China's Currency Reform Was Not Instigated by the UK 27

Roos Did Not Propose a Loan to China to Japan Either. All Countries Benefit from the Stability of Chinese Finance

(London) It is rumored that Japan intends to reply to the UK, refusing to participate in the international loan to China, because China did not consult with Japan first before announcing currency reform. People in London were surprised by this news. China's currency reform was neither instigated by the UK nor due to British assistance. Although representatives of the UK, Japan, and the United States had experimental discussions on the matter of international loans to China, since Sir Arthur Salter, the economic advisor to the British government, traveled to the Far East, the UK has not put forward specific measures regarding loans to China to Japan. Therefore, people in London felt that it was even more strange that Japan intended to send a note to the UK during this discussion phase, solemnly declaring its unwillingness to participate in international loans to China. The Japanese warlords' recognition of the UK's loan to China as an accomplished fact has received considerable attention from the British press today, but the British government may not attach much importance to it. According to responsible sources, the UK has not proposed a separate loan to China, because the UK is aware of its obligations to the banking group and cannot take this step without long and careful consideration. Today's editorial in The Times calls for a purely monetary plan. It is a pity if the Japanese insist on objecting in error and accuse it of having political implications. It should be known that if currency and financial reforms can be effectively adopted, then not only China will benefit from the more stable Chinese financial system, but all countries that have business relations with China, especially Japan, will benefit from it as well. (12th Reuters)

(Tokyo) After the British government submitted a notification to the Japanese government regarding the issue of China's currency reform and joint loans to China by various countries, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Finance decided to hold a meeting within the next few days to formulate a reply. When Ambassador to China Arichi met with British Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen, and Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Shigemitsu met with British Ambassador to Japan Clive, they clarified the Japanese government's official views on currency reform and joint loans. Current Commentary

Dedication to the Fifth National Congress 32

— Tao

The Fifth National Congress opened yesterday. There were more representatives from various regions than in previous sessions, which is a sign of internal unity and progress within the Kuomintang. The National Congress is the highest authority of the Kuomintang and has the power to change and decide on the party constitution and platform. At the same time, it is the only body to elect the 5th Central Executive Committee. Therefore, its mission is more important than the usual Central Committee plenary session. It is also because of this that it bears a heavier responsibility to the party and the nation. Here, we sincerely hope that all the attending officials can recognize their mission and responsibilities and console the ardent hopes of the people.

Today, the people of the country can be said to have accepted the Kuomintang's doctrine and principles in principle and mostly deeply believe that they are the only way to build the country. What they are not satisfied with is that although the Kuomintang has a brilliant and bright doctrine and platform, it has failed to earnestly promote and fulfill them as soon as possible. For example, restricting capital and equalizing land ownership are the essence of the Kuomintang's Principle of People's Livelihood. However, in the past seven or eight years, has there been anything similar to this kind of policy? The most important mass training during the period of political tutelage is the training of the four rights. However, after six years of political tutelage, it has not been possible to do this. Other grand plans that can be spoken of but not acted upon are also countless. We know that the occurrence of this phenomenon is mostly due to the internal and external troubles that have plagued us in recent years and the lack of both human and financial resources. However, the Kuomintang's failure to make its best efforts and the lack of enthusiasm among ordinary party members to promote the doctrine should not fail to be a major reason. How to remedy these abuses and make amends, and strive to save the situation, is what the officials attending the conference today should pay attention to and carefully plan for.

The national crisis is no greater than it is today. The Kuomintang is at the forefront of this crisis and has become the target of criticism. For a time, celebrities and scholars mostly advocated ending political tutelage as soon as possible and opening up the party ban, as if there was no other way to save the country. However, in all fairness, China's current national crisis is the culmination of the accumulation of historical events in recent decades and cannot be solely blamed on the Kuomintang. Even if the Kuomintang immediately handed over power today, we dare to assert that China's national crisis would not only not necessarily be alleviated, but might even be aggravated. Why? Today's national crisis is mostly due to the fact that our country does not have the conditions of a modern country. The Kuomintang has a history of several decades and hundreds of thousands of party members. Its doctrines and policies are all major principles and laws that are indispensable for building a modern country. If such a party holds the national power and still cannot achieve anything, and it is said that handing over this power to other temporary small political groups of three or two people can make the country come back to life, who can believe it if they are not foolish and tasteless? Therefore, those who can truly understand the truth should not attribute the severity of the national crisis to the Kuomintang. However, in order to live up to the trust of the people, the Kuomintang should make its various checks redeemable as soon as possible.

Responding to League of Nations Sanctions, Italy Launches a Twofold Counterattack: Protesting to Sanctioning Countries on One Hand, and Implementing Import Controls and Retaliation on the Other 33

(Rome) Mussolini has retaliated against the sanctions passed by the League of Nations. In addition to sending notes to the countries participating in the sanctions, attacking the legal basis of the League of Nations' actions, the Italian government has also promulgated a royal decree temporarily suspending trade relations with the countries implementing sanctions and deciding to implement it from November 18, the date the League of Nations' economic war begins. (11th National Telegram)

(Rome) The Italian government has sent a note to the governments of all member states of the League of Nations Adjustment Committee on the sanctions plan, and a copy of the original text has been sent to the governments of other countries for reference. The content is as follows: (1) Italy denies violating Article 12 of the League of Nations Covenant, so the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy are not fair. (Article 12 of the Covenant stipulates that if a dispute arises between member states, they may not engage in war until three months after the Executive Council's report, etc.) (2) The people of Abyssinia and the local authorities, as well as religious leaders, are willing to accept Italian protection. After the Italian army occupied the city of Adowa, it ordered the abolition of the slave system in the occupied territories and has fulfilled the obligations of an advanced country. (3) The League of Nations did not notify Italy of the procedures for implementing sanctions under Article 16 of the Covenant. (4) Sanctions will not only endanger the Italian economy, but also seriously affect the world economy. In order to safeguard the survival of its nation, Italy will inevitably take self-defense measures to ensure that the goods needed by the Italian people are not in short supply, and the current relations of international trade must be disintegrated as a result. In short, although the prohibition of the import of all goods from Italy by various countries is an economic measure, it is actually a truly hostile act. Italy has sufficient reason to take retaliatory measures. The League of Nations' move attempts to exclude the 44 million people of Italy from the world market. Once Italy implements retaliation, millions of farmers around the world will be unable to make a living as a result. (5) Although the League of Nations holds an opposing attitude towards Italy, Italy has no intention of withdrawing from the League of Nations in order to avoid causing more serious disputes. The Italian government has taken all measures to prevent the crisis that this situation may cause. "But the member states of the League of Nations are requested to pay attention to the issue of responsibility that may be caused by the implementation of sanctions." Finally, it is said that the Italian government will deal with the coercive measures taken by various countries against Italy calmly. (12th Havas)

UK Attitude Remains Unchanged 34

(London) Although the Italian government has protested to the governments of the countries participating in the sanctions on the issue of implementing sanctions, according to what our reporter knows, the attitude of the British government has not changed as a result. All economic sanctions will take effect according to the date proposed by the British government, i.e., the 18th of this month. (12th Havas)

Interview Between Italy and Laval Intended 35

(Paris) The Italian Ambassador to France today held an important conversation with the Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval. The content of the conversation was not disclosed. Officials believe the main topic was Italy's attitude towards the League of Nations' sanctions. Although officials anticipate Italy will take the strictest retaliatory measures against countries implementing sanctions, it has been confirmed that Italy will not prohibit imports from sanctioning countries nor rescind existing trade agreements. It is said the Italian government will issue a statement tomorrow regarding countermeasures to sanctions. (Havas dispatch, November 11)

Note to the US is Informational 36

(Washington) The Italian Ambassador to the United States, Rosso, met with Under Secretary of State Phillips today and later expressed the opinion that the United States has no connection to the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy. (National Telegram, November 11)

(Washington) The Italian Ambassador to the United States, Rosso, spoke with Under Secretary of State Phillips today and handed him a copy of the Italian note to the League of Nations Sanctions Committee. The note requests each country to declare its position on economic sanctions. However, for the United States, it is merely for informational purposes and does not expect a response. Rosso also stated that the note does not mention the US neutrality law or measures taken because of it. Rosso briefly described the contents of the note to reporters, which include the following six points: (1) Italy does not acknowledge violating the League of Nations Covenant and strongly protests the injustice of the sanctions. (2) Italy declares that all events since the last meeting of the League of Nations Council and Assembly have proven Italy's claim that Abyssinia is morally unfit to be a member of the League of Nations. (3) The actions of the Sanctions Committee are illegal because the committee is not a legitimate organization of the League of Nations. (4) The arms embargo on Italy, but not on Abyssinia, has exacerbated the situation in East Africa. (5) Sanctions were not implemented during the conflicts in Daba Valley and Manchuria. (6) Boycotting Italian goods is an act of war, and Italy can take retaliatory action. (National Telegram, November 11)

Italian Government Orders Control of Foreign Imports 37

Wide Range of Goods Included As Retaliation Against Sanctioning Nations

(Rome) Last night, the government ordered the control of foreign imports to retaliate against the countries implementing sanctions against Italy. According to the order's provisions, starting November 18, importers purchasing copper, iron, meat, coffee, grains, cotton, single-wrap silk, hardware, and other various goods from foreign countries must obtain a license from the government. The scope is very broad, almost including all goods. (Reuters dispatch, December 12)

(Rome) The government has just issued an order stipulating that, starting from the 18th of this month (the date when various countries will implement economic sanctions against Italy), anyone importing the following goods into Italy must first obtain government permission and the government will determine the quantity to be imported. These goods are meat, grains, oilseed, oils, fatty foods, woven fabrics, silk fabrics, metal ores, chemical and medical instruments, tanning and dyeing supplies, pigments, rubber, hides, furs, pulp, paper, gramophones, jewelry, gemstones, precious metals, and films. However, currency notes and books are not included. The above measures also apply to the Libyan territories in Africa. In addition, the government has issued an order stipulating that office hours for all agencies will be from 9:00 AM to 4:30 PM, with only a half-hour break in the middle, to advance time and save on electricity bills. Finally, the government has another order stipulating that the original tax rate will be maintained for income tax on small amounts of money, but for those with higher incomes, it will be moderately increased starting January 1, 1937. (Havas dispatch, December 12)

Luring the Enemy Deep into the Interior Ethiopian Troops Await at Leisure 38

Sufficient Ammunition and Provisions Preparing for a Protracted War

(Rome) Italian troops are now asking each other where the Ethiopian troops will make a stand and defend themselves. According to reports from both the northern and southern fronts, the Italian troops' operations are no different from striking air. Although the Italian troops advance quickly, the Ethiopian troops retreat even faster. Whenever the Italian troops enter a town, they find no enemy soldiers. It is generally believed that the Ethiopian troops' strategy is to lure the Italian troops deep into more rugged terrain, lengthen their lines of communication, and then rely on advantageous terrain to await the enemy at leisure and engage with them. Currently, it is believed that the Ethiopian troops on the northern front will persist in resistance south of Ambalagi. Italian aircraft reconnaissance flights have spotted a large army of over 100,000 men gathering in that area. On the southern front, Ethiopian troops are expected to defend along the Qiqiqa to Harar line. (Reuters dispatch, November 11)

(Rome) According to military experts here, the Ethiopian troops' repeated retreats are motivated by two factors. One is to force Italy to lengthen its lines of communication, and the other is to lure the Italian troops deep into the Ethiopian interior, where the Ethiopian troops have stockpiled large quantities of ammunition and food, making it easy to wage a protracted war against the Italian troops. Ethiopia is currently repairing roads from the western provinces to the Xuya province (northeast of the capital). After the road is repaired, Ethiopian reinforcements from the rear will easily arrive in an endless stream. Conversely, Italian troops advancing from the northern front must simultaneously build roads and establish transportation and rear bases. The reason for the slow progress of the Italian troops in the Tigray province lies in this. It is said that the Ethiopian troops are preparing to confront 220,000 Italian troops in southern Tigray, including 50,000 men led by General Seyoum, 70,000 men led by General Qasa, 50,000 men led by General Yngala, and 70,000 men of the Ethiopian Imperial Guard. All of these troops are equipped with modern weapons and concentrated along the Taquesse River. In addition, Crown Prince Asfaw Wossen is stationing another 40,000 men between the city of Taixi and Lake Achanki to resist the advance of the Italian left wing. (Havas dispatch, November 11)

Addis Ababa A clergyman arrived here today from the Tigray region, claiming that the morale of the Ethiopian troops in the Danping area is very high. He also said that although the Italian troops have appointed Qufsa, an Ethiopian leader who surrendered to Italy, as the civil administrator of Magal, the people of Tigray also know that they will never accept Qufsa's rule. According to a dispatch from the southern front, the Italian troops used tear gas in the battle to capture Golahai. (Reuters dispatch, November 11)

Armistice Day President Roosevelt's Declaration Willing to Strive for World Peace 46

Trade Barriers Are a Cause of International Conflict Aggressive Ambitions Do Not Obstruct Human Progress Treaties Treated as Trifles Where is International Credit?

(Washington) In his Armistice Day speech at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier today, President Roosevelt made an important announcement regarding Britain's world policy. President Roosevelt pointed out that trade barriers are a cause of international conflict and declared that the United States and Canada have effectively agreed to eliminate differences regarding unreasonable trade restrictions. President Roosevelt also solemnly stated that the United States is willing to always seek peaceful means, but must protect itself. The more other countries reduce their armaments, the faster and more firmly the United States will carry out its disarmament. Except for a very small number of people who value private interests over the peace of the nation and the world, the vast majority of the American people unanimously support the government's basic policies in this regard and fully sympathize with other countries' efforts to eliminate war. This is why we have always diligently supported steps to eliminate the causes of war and opposed the aggressive actions taken by other countries. We have used concrete actions and solemn promises to make the United States a good friend. We call the armed aggression and killing acts of people war, and give war a simple definition and reality. We acknowledge that the world's progress has been minimal, which disappoints us. The dangers faced by the entire mankind in the future are greater than those faced by the American people alone. International jealousy still exists, the increase in armaments and the ambitions of countries that disturb the peace have not yet been suppressed, and the most significant crisis is that international trust in the sacred solemnity of international contracts is now weakening. We cannot build walls around ourselves or bury our heads in the sand, we can only move forward with all our strength to seek international peace. (Reuters dispatch, November 11)

US Army Officer Successfully Ascends Stratosphere Achieves Record of 74,000 Feet Above Ground 48

Weiner A stratosphere balloon rose to 74,187 feet today, about fifteen miles, breaking the high-altitude record. It landed near the small town of Sticker, eleven miles north of Platt. The metal ship was not shaken when it landed. Explorers Captain Stevens and Anderson completed fifteen kinds of scientific experiments at an altitude of fourteen miles above sea level. The mysterious nature of the stratosphere may be understood more clearly. The balloon landed very quickly. As the sun was setting, the 3.5 million cubic feet of helium slowly leaked out, and the balloon gradually shrank, losing its buoyancy. When the balloon approached the ground, the people in the balloon climbed to the top of the metal ship. Captain Stevens threw a long rope from above and tied it to a tree on the ground. The rope was slowly lowered, and the metal wheel landed safely after two minutes. Four US Army airplanes that followed the balloon also landed at the site a few minutes later. The people in the planes helped the two fold the balloon and sort out the instruments in preparation for transportation. The two were successful and in good spirits. Captain Stevens, who managed the instruments, declared that once the instruments were inspected, it would be known that they had risen to a height of 74,000 feet to 75,000 feet. The landing site was near a highway, and thousands of curious people gathered there in an instant, repeatedly trying to get close to the balloon to find souvenirs, but they were stopped by the air force personnel. The metal ship was made of manganese alloy lighter than aluminum. The shell was only three-sixteenths of an inch thick, but it was extremely hard. The two observed the ascent through many round holes. One hole allowed them to see the shape of the balloon, another hole allowed Anderson to see the ground, and there was another hole under the metal ship, equipped with a large camera, which took pictures every minute and a half. The side of the ship had holes for radio equipment, which the people in the ship used to communicate with the ground. The ship and instruments weighed a total of six tons, and the balloon weighed three tons. (National Telegram, November 11)

Tanchen The two American Army majors, Stevens and Anderson, returned after ascending to a height of 72,000 feet on the world's largest balloon "Explorer II", and landed at White Lake today, 230 miles from Tanchen, breaking the world record for altitude. "Explorer II" took off this morning for stratospheric investigation, spending about eight hours in the sky, taking four hours and twenty-five minutes to ascend and three hours and eight minutes to descend. At 3:20 PM, the balloon sent a radio report that it had reached an altitude of 60,000 feet, and the temperature outside the balloon was 67 degrees below zero. The balloon's goal of 70,000 feet was soon reached, and it continued to ascend for another thousand feet before beginning to descend. When the balloon descended to a thousand feet above the ground, the two explorers climbed to the top of the balloon chamber to prepare for the most important part of the landing. Finally, it landed safely at White Lake. The average descent speed was 400 feet per minute. In addition to the X-ray recorder, the two majors, Shi and An, also used other new photographic and perspective devices to take pictures of the earth at various altitudes. The previous official world altitude record was 61,236.691 feet, set by two American Navy officers, Settle and Fordney, on November 29, 1933. On January 31 of the following year, three Russian pilots reached a height of 67,954 feet, but unfortunately, the balloon chamber fell off during the descent, crashing to the ground, and all the pilots died. Although their results exceeded those of their predecessors, they were not included in the official record. (Reuters dispatch, November 11)

Guangdong Province Strictly Prohibits the Outflow of Silver 49

Additional Restrictions on the Transportation of Silver Coins At the Same Time, the Government Uses Legal Tender to Collect Hard Currency

Guangzhou Communication After the promulgation of the currency management laws in Guangdong Province, silver coins in general have lost their circulation effectiveness. In order to prevent the outflow of silver, on the one hand, in accordance with the laws, provincial and municipal silver small denomination notes and silver dollar legal tender are used to purchase silver coins and silver dollar coins at an increased rate (that is, small denomination notes and legal tender of one dollar and two cents are used to purchase one dollar of silver coins, and silver dollar legal tender of one dollar and forty-four cents are used to purchase one silver dollar hard currency), so as to concentrate the silver in the government. On the other hand, strict prevention and precaution are taken against merchants privately transporting silver for export. Regarding the issuance of permits for transporting silver, the Department of Finance has added regulations, which have been submitted to the provincial government for approval and implementation. The following eight temporary measures, which the Department of Finance has added to restrict the transportation of silver coins within the province and the issuance of permits, are recorded below:

1. If merchants in this province transport small denomination silver dollars or silver dollars to areas that have always used small denomination silver dollars or silver dollars, and the vessels carrying them must pass through the ocean for export before re-importing to the destination, or belong to the domestic border, they can leave the country upon arrival. Even if the transporters are not directly smuggling for export, but there is a possibility of circumventing export for profit, in addition to the allowable limit of ten yuan per the silver prohibition rules, if there is more, it will be handled in accordance with the supplementary measures previously ordered by this department to crack down on private transportation of hard currency circumventing export from the inland, and the provisions of these measures.

2. If there is no situation mentioned in the preceding article (1) for transporting silver coins within the province, these measures do not apply.

3. If there is a situation mentioned in the preceding article (1) for transporting silver coins within the province, the person should, in accordance with the supplementary measures, find a reputable and well-established guarantee shop in Guangzhou that has obtained a business license to provide a guarantee bond and submit it to the Department of Finance for verification, approval, and issuance of a permit to protect the transport of silver. If the Department of Finance has entrusted the customs supervision office or customs branch to issue transport permits on its behalf, the local area will still handle it in accordance with the case.

4. Whether silver coins are transported for export or import, they are limited to locations where customs offices are established. No matter which ferry is used to carry the silver coins, it must be listed on the manifest of the ferry for customs inspection and verification.

5. When declaring for import, the permit should be submitted to the customs for inspection. After the customs has completed the verification, the date of verification and release should be written on the permit, stamped with a seal, and released. After being transported to the destination, the reporting merchant should submit the permit to the original issuing agency for verification and cancellation within the time limit.

6. Regardless of which agency issues the permit to protect the transport, this department may at any time secretly order officials of the local agency to investigate whether a merchant has transported silver coins to the local area and sold them abroad to smuggle them for export and profit. If there is such a situation, even if the original protection permit has been cancelled, the guarantee shop and the reporting merchant cannot shirk their responsibility.

7. Wuzhou is an inland commercial port outside this province, but the commercial relationship between Guangdong and Wuzhou is close. These measures specifically treat Wuzhou in the same way as the inland areas of this province. If there is a merchant transporting silver from Guangzhou to Wuzhou, the reason for needing to transport silver should be submitted to this department for the issuance of a permit before transportation can begin.

8. These measures will be promulgated and implemented by the Department of Finance after being submitted to the provincial government and transferred to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee for the customs supervisors and tax commissioners of this province to follow, and the various customs offices will implement them in accordance with the instructions. (November 7)

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

How Do the Sun, Moon, and Stars Move, and What Phenomena Result from Their Movements? (5) 52

— (Lectures to the National Public on October 18th, 21st, 27th, and 28th) Researcher at the Institute of Astronomy, Academia Sinica Chen Zun-Gui

I have now checked that from 1542 AD (the 21st year of the Ming Dynasty's Jiajing reign) to this year, in roughly 400 years, there have been a total of 26 solar eclipses that passed over China. From this year onwards, in 100 years, there will be a total of 10 total solar eclipses visible in China, which can be considered a very plentiful century. However, these solar eclipses may either be too close to dawn, too close to sunset, or too far towards the northern or southern borders. Seeking those whose position is just right to be visible at noon, in the past 400 years there have only been 4, and in the next 100 years, there will only be one, which roughly matches the estimated odds above. If we also require that they pass through densely populated areas along the Yellow River and Yangtze River, and be visible near noon in the central region of the mainland, then in 500 years, there will only be two. One is the total eclipse of August 11, 1542 (the day of Ji You in the seventh month of the 21st year of the Ming Dynasty's Jiajing reign, as recorded in the History of Ming), a noon solar eclipse in the Yellow River basin. The second is the total eclipse of September 21, 1941 (the 30th year of the Republic of China), a noon solar eclipse in the Yangtze River basin. These two total eclipses are almost exactly four centuries apart. Such an opportunity can truly be considered rare and precious, so our country's astronomers, physicists, and meteorologists have now organized a Solar Eclipse Observation Committee to prepare for the observation activities at that time.

The most recent total solar eclipses visible in our China were originally the two on June 19th of next year and February 5th of the 32nd year of the Republic of China (1943 AD), but the paths of these two are both very far towards the northeastern borders, so the opportunity is not very good. There is also one on May 9th of the 37th year of the Republic of China (1948 AD), although it is from southwest to northeast, most of what will be visible is an annular eclipse, and even if a little total eclipse can be seen, the time will be extremely short.

What I have said above is the situation of solar and lunar eclipses that occur as a result of the movement of the sun and moon. Now we want to talk about the changes of the four seasons.

What are the four seasons? We all know that they are spring, summer, autumn, and winter. We also know that summer is very hot, winter is very cold, and spring and autumn are warm and suitable. So everyone knows that spring, summer, autumn, and winter are related to climate and temperature. But how do spring, summer, autumn, and winter occur? Why do the temperatures of each season change? That is related to the position of the sun, or in other words, it is because the Earth revolves around the sun.

We all know that the Earth is a oblate spheroid shape, and it rotates once every day. Its rotation method is to rotate around a line passing through its center as an axis. For example, if we take a wooden ball and insert a wooden rod through the center of the wooden ball, and we hold both ends of the wooden rod with two hands and rotate it, then the wooden ball will also rotate with it. The Earth's rotation is the same as this style. The line passing through the center of the Earth is called the axis of rotation, and the two ends of the axis of rotation are called the poles. The plane perpendicular to the axis of rotation intersects the Earth's surface to form a large circle, and this large circle is called the Earth's equator. Therefore, we connect the points on the Earth's surface that are equidistant from the two poles, and that is the Earth's equator. For example, the wooden ball mentioned above represents our Earth. We use a pencil to connect all the points on the surface of the ball that are equidistant from the two ends of the rod, and that must be a large circle, and this circle is the equator.

When we stand outside in the yard, we see the sky as if it is a hemispherical shape. All the sun, moon, and stars seem to be on this hemisphere. In reality, this sky is a large sphere centered on where we are standing, with an infinitely large length as its radius. Although we only see half of it, the other half is below our horizon. This large sphere is called the celestial sphere in astronomy. All the movements of the sun, moon, and stars are imagined on top of this celestial sphere. We assume that we extend the Earth's equator outwards, and it must intersect the celestial sphere in a large circle called the celestial equator. We extend the two ends of the Earth's axis of rotation outwards, and it must intersect the celestial sphere at two points, the one in the north is called the north celestial pole, and the one in the south is called the south celestial pole. Near the north celestial pole there is a star that we call the North Star. On a clear night, we stand facing north, first find the location of the Big Dipper. After seeing the Big Dipper, then extend the two stars on the outside of the Dipper towards the mouth of the Dipper, to about five times the distance between these two stars, there is a bright star, and that is the North Star. The north celestial pole is near this star, which is also the direction pointed to by our Earth's axis of rotation.

We already know that the Earth revolves around the sun, but when we look from the Earth, it seems that the sun is the machine that is moving in the sky. The time it takes for our Earth to actually revolve around the sun once is called a year, and the orbit it travels projected onto the celestial sphere is called the ecliptic. Therefore, the ecliptic is the orbit traveled by the sun on the celestial sphere in a year. This ecliptic and the equator are not the same, the angle at which they intersect is twenty-three and a half degrees. Because these two large circles—the equator is a large circle, and the ecliptic is also a large circle—are not the same, they intersect at two points, and these two points are called the equinoxes, which are the vernal equinox and the autumnal equinox.

Since the ecliptic and the equator are not on the same plane, the ecliptic is divided into two parts by the equator, one part is to the north of the equator, and one part is to the south of the equator. We know that the sun travels on the ecliptic, so every year the sun enters and exits the north and south of the equator, that is, it travels from the north side of the equator to the south side of the equator, and then travels from the south side to the north side of the equator, once a year. Therefore, there are two dates each year when the sun is above the equator, which are the dates when it passes through the two equinoxes. One is around March 21st each year, when the sun travels from the southern hemisphere to the northern hemisphere, and the point it passes is called the vernal equinox, and this time is called the vernal equinox. The other is around September 23rd each year, when the sun travels from the northern hemisphere to the southern hemisphere, and the point it passes is called the autumnal equinox, and this time is called the autumnal equinox. Also, the lowest point on the ecliptic south of the equator is called the winter solstice point, and the time when the sun is at this point is called the winter solstice. The highest point on the ecliptic north of the equator is called the summer solstice point, and the time when the sun is at this point is called the summer solstice.

As for the direction of sunrise and sunset, it is also different in the four seasons. In the case of China, during the vernal equinox and autumnal equinox, the sun rises from due east and sets in due west. The path traveled by the sun in one day, half is above the horizon and half is below the horizon, so day and night are equal, that is, daytime and nighttime are the same length. At the summer solstice, the sun is in the far north, rising from the northeast direction and setting in the northwest. The path traveled by the sun on the horizon is larger than a semicircle, so the daytime is the longest and the nighttime is the shortest. At the winter solstice, the sun is in the far south, rising from the southeast direction and setting in the southwest. The path traveled by the sun above the horizon is smaller than a semicircle, so the daytime is the shortest and the nighttime is the longest.

The sun travels eastward along the ecliptic from around March 21st of this year, after passing the vernal equinox point, until around March 21st of next year when it passes the vernal equinox point again, which is one year. In this year, the sun travels one circle on the ecliptic, a total of 360 degrees; the four points mentioned above, the vernal equinox, summer solstice, autumnal equinox, and winter solstice, are exactly 90 degrees apart from each other. Then divide 90 degrees into six equal parts, with 15 degrees as one segment, for a total of twenty-four solar terms. Their order, starting from the vernal equinox, is the vernal equinox, Qingming (Pure Brightness), Guyu (Grain Rain), Lixia (Start of Summer), Xiaoman (Grain Full), Mangzhong (Grain in Ear), summer solstice, Xiaoshu (Minor Heat), Dashu (Major Heat), Liqiu (Start of Autumn), Chushu (End of Heat), Bailu (White Dew), autumnal equinox, Hanlu (Cold Dew), Shuangjiang (Frost's Descent), Lidong (Start of Winter), Xiaoxue (Minor Snow), Daxue (Major Snow), winter solstice, Xiaohan (Minor Cold), Dahan (Major Cold), Lichun (Start of Spring), Yushui (Rain Water), Jingzhe (Awakening of Insects). The source of these twenty-four solar terms, according to the solar terms mentioned above, is completely based on the position of the sun, so many people think that the solar terms are the benefit of the solar calendar, which is really ridiculous. Regarding this issue, I will talk about it next time when I talk about "the benefits of the National Calendar". As for the division of the four seasons, some are divided according to the solar terms, and some are divided according to the climate. His decree can be divided into three types

First, the division method that we have always used in China is

Spring: With the vernal equinox as the center, that is, from Lichun (around February 4th) to Lixia (around May 5th or 6th), a total of ninety days and eighteen hours.

Summer: With the summer solstice as the center, that is, from Lixia to Liqiu (around August 7th or 8th), a total of ninety-four days and one hour.

Autumn: With the autumnal equinox as the center, that is, from Liqiu to Lidong (around November 7th), a total of ninety-one days and twenty hours.

Winter: With the winter solstice as the center, that is, from Lidong to Lichun, a total of eighty-eight days and fifteen hours.

That is, we Chinese use the four "Li" (establishment) characters as the beginning of the four seasons, that is, Lichun is the beginning of spring, Lixia is the beginning of summer. Our Chinese lunar calendar stipulates that the first, second, and third months are the spring season. However, the number of days in each month is determined by the new moon and full moon, and the number of months is determined according to the position of the sun, so the first day of the first month is not necessarily Lichun. Lichun is often around fourteen and a half days before or after the first day of the first month, so Lichun is sometimes at the end of the previous year, but the average over a long period is probably around the ninth day of the first month.

Second, the division method of Western countries is

Spring: From the vernal equinox (around March 21st or 22nd) to the summer solstice (around June 22nd or 23rd), a total of ninety-two days and twenty hours.

Summer: From the summer solstice to the autumnal equinox (around September 22nd or 23rd), a total of ninety-three days and fourteen hours.

Autumn: From the autumnal equinox to the winter solstice (around December 21st or 22nd), a total of eighty-nine days and nineteen hours.

Winter: From the winter solstice to the vernal equinox, a total of eighty-nine days and one hour. The above division method is commonly called the astronomers' division method. It is called spring from the date of equal day and night in late March to the date of the longest day. From the end of spring to the date of equal day and night in September, it is called summer, from the end of summer to the date of the shortest day it is called autumn, from the end of autumn to the date of equal day and night next year, it is called winter

Third, the division of the weather fruit. is

Spring: March, April, May, three months, a total of ninety-two days

Summer: June, July, August, three months, a total of ninety-two days

Autumn: September, October, November, three months, a total of ninety-one days

Winter:, December, January, February, three months, a total of ninety days or ninety-one days

Bank-issued banknotes guaranteed by real estate, with denominations of one yuan, five yuan, and ten yuan, total about 1.3 million yuan in circulation in the market. (3) After the bank's closure, the unrecovered guaranteed banknotes are circulated with the Chamber of Commerce's seal, called circulating notes, with about 600,000 yuan still in the market. In addition, there are temporary white paper subsidiary currency notes issued for year-end turnover (i.e., day exchange orders, with face values of 50 yuan and 100 yuan), which were originally limited to short-term circulation and were to be recovered within the period, but in fact, various stores have formed long-term use due to credit or business relationships, in order to facilitate mutual assistance and settlement among peers. In addition, various reputable stores in Chao'an, Chenghai, Jieyang, Puning, and Chaoyang counties, such as those that have obtained the status of gentry from district and township chiefs, also print and issue silver dollar and copper cash notes, with denominations of 50 cents, 100 cents, 5 dimes, and 10 dimes, which are entrusted to collection and exchange shops in Shantou for cash redemption, so they can also circulate. The total number cannot be investigated, because there are many shops and numbers in each county, and the printing and issuance are not subject to government inspection, nor is there a board of directors to protect them. With such a chaotic and complex situation, the intangible losses of the people cannot be quantified.

The Shantou branch of the Provincial Bank is a sub-treasury for collecting provincial and national taxes. The monthly tax revenue from Chaozhou and Meizhou submitted to the bank is no less than 2 million yuan. With sufficient capital and good credit, it issues 5-dime, 1-yuan, 5-yuan, and 10-yuan silver dollar notes, totaling about 800,000 yuan. Also, because Shantou markets circulate silver dollars, it separately issues 300,000 yuan of silver dollar notes. The banknotes issued by the Shantou Provincial Bank are printed with the words "Shantou", and the style is the same as the banknotes of the Guangzhou head office, but the price is different. In previous political upheavals and rumors in Guangdong Province, the price of Provincial Bank banknotes fluctuated, but the price of the banknotes of the Shantou branch has always been stable and has not deviated from the standard, because silver dollars and silver dimes are not as convenient as Provincial Bank banknotes for carrying, settlement, and paying taxes. Moreover, Provincial Bank banknotes must first be exchanged for silver dimes at exchange shops and require a premium to be used in Shantou, because the banknotes of the head office cannot be directly circulated and used in Chaoshan, which is the difference. Before the Ministry of Finance's order on nationalization of silver reached Shantou, the Shantou branch of the Provincial Bank actually held the highest authority in the city's financial circles. As for the Central Bank, Bank of Communications, and the two banks, there are no branches in Chaoshan. The Shantou branch of the Bank of China only operates domestic and foreign exchange, savings, etc., and collects taxes on behalf of the Chaozhou Customs. Banknotes from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are very rare in Chaoshan. Someone remits money from Shanghai to Shantou through the Bank of China, and a 35-yuan remittance note only receives about 32 yuan in Shantou. The exchange rate and silver price are so far apart. If legal tender is brought from Shanghai to Shantou for use, it must first be exploited by the exchange shops, and it will probably only get 92%. This can also be seen as the currency situation in Chaoshan in the past.

On the 7th of this month, the Finance Department promulgated the order on nationalization of silver to Shantou, and the method is the same as that promulgated by the Ministry of Finance, but the Bank of China collects Chaozhou Customs taxes using the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications banknotes as the standard, and the Shantou branch of the Provincial Bank collects various taxes using the Provincial Bank banknotes as the standard, and the Provincial Bank banknotes use the Shantou local name notes as the standard, so there are in effect two countries' legal tender in Chaoshan markets. The financial situation in Chaoshan still feels chaotic, and due to the major financial turbulence in recent days, prices have soared, and the people are also very distressed.

In the Zhongzhuang Township of the First District, more than 200 guest籍 refugees arrived on the day of Er. They stayed in the Huangchi Temple that night. The next morning, they went to the Shenjiawan area to rope in rice and other grains, and robbed the house of Baozhang (Neighborhood chief) Chen Dingxing, where they were robbed of three fur coats.
