Nantong

Burning Cotton Stalks to Eliminate Pests

In recent years, the counties under the jurisdiction of Jiangbei Tong and the coastal reclamation areas have suffered from insect pests, and production has decreased. According to research by cotton pest experts, the nests of these pests for overwintering are mostly lurking in cotton stalks, dead leaves, or fruit bolls, and only become active in March and April of the following spring. The villagers use cotton stalks as fuel and are unwilling to burn them in the fields, which is against the prestige of insect pests. They are encouraging the villagers to burn the cotton stalks beforehand and limit all states to be burned before Qingming next year. Special orders were issued to each county to make use of Baojia to implement it effectively.

Yangzhou

Villagers from Three Counties Sue Each Other Over a Judgment

The villagers from the same township in Zhenjiangyi three counties previously sued because Xiao Wensun and Zhang Dongchen, from the same township in Yangzhou, dismantled the Nanmu Hall wood of the Hubei Guild Hall and transported it to Jin Da Wood Company outside Fuyunmen for sale. This was discovered by fellow villager Dan Gongjin, who reported it to the Public Security Bureau, which ordered the first sub-station to send police to stop it. At the same time, brick lawyer Fang Ren wrote a complaint to the court, requesting the restoration of the original state. After several trials by Judge Zhou of the Civil Court, a judgment was pronounced a few days ago. The main text said that the Wang Bucheng and others' resolution on February 19 of this year was confirmed to be invalid. The defendants Xiao Wensun and Zhang Dongchen should restore the dismantled part of the Nanmu Hall of the Hubei Guild Hall to its original state, and the rest of the plaintiff's claims were rejected. The litigation costs were to be borne by the defendant.

Yuyao

Livelihoods of Salt Farmers Amidst the Salt Tide

The Yuyao salt field is the best in Zhejiang, producing a large amount of salt. It has a salt factory that specializes in buying and selling salt and selling it to various provinces. The business has always been known to be developed. Since the beginning of this year, the salt works have been piling up with stock, losing money for years, and not accepting new goods. Therefore, the livelihoods of 100,000 salt farmers have been cut off. If they sell smuggled goods, there are prohibitions in the law, and the salt farmers dare not try it lightly, resulting in the sale of wives and children, which is often heard. There are several suicides and starvation deaths a day. In this situation, the salt farmers were forced to gather in groups and ask the salt works to open scales and accept salt several times to maintain their livelihoods. However, the manager of the salt works had already fled, and no one was responsible, so there was no answer. Fortunately, Salt Transport Envoy Zhou Zonghua saw the seriousness of the situation, so he convened a meeting of salt merchants. As a result, the salt works were notified to collect salt at 60% of the reported amount, but the salt farmers felt that it was still difficult to maintain their livelihoods and could not be satisfied. Later, after strenuous persuasion, some who were forced into poverty only sold it painfully, and there were still some who sat and waited for death. I don't know how many there are, it is said.

Wenzhou

Security Forces Rescue Hostages

The Security Corps of Zhaitou, the third district of Yuhuan, received a tip-off on the afternoon of the 7th of this month that two hostages were hidden in the Sutou Suyan Cave in the local mountains. Squad Leader Fu immediately led the troops to search. Halfway there, they suddenly met a child who asked if the hostage Sun Renzhou, 14 years old, from the Chetou of Yueqing Baixiang, and his classmate Huang Lihua, (11 years old) were sleeping in the cave. They took the opportunity to escape while the bandits were drinking and hadn't returned. He was young and unable to walk, crying and lost. He thought that he was still in the hands of thieves. There were more than ten other classmates. Because the bandits were inconvenient to carry due to the strict pursuit of the military and police, they were all pushed into the sea by the bandits and drowned, which is pitiful. Squad Leader Fu wrote a detailed document based on the situation and sent it to the Chuli Corps headquarters in person, and telegraphed to Yueqing County Magistrate Zhang to inform the family members to come and claim them.

Western Travels and Observations 53

— Jiyuan

Various Aspects of Chongqing (Part 1)

Chongqing is located between the Yangtze River and the Jialing River, the entire city forming a peninsula. Houses are built against the mountains, varying in height. Geographically speaking, it is quite similar to Los Angeles in the United States and Hong Kong in southern China. However, in terms of the narrowness of the streets and the disorder on the streets, it is far inferior. According to recent statistics, the city has a population of over 300,000, and including Jiangbei and Ba County, about 800,000, making it the largest commercial port in Sichuan and a strategic barrier for both northwestern and southwestern China. Except for a portion of goods from Lower Eastern Sichuan that are distributed from Wanxian, most of Sichuan's import and export trade must pass through Chongqing as a transportation hub. The import and export goods of provinces such as Yunnan, Guizhou, Xikang, Shaanxi, and Gansu are also mostly transshipped here.

Due to its strategic location, as early as the sixteenth year of the Guangxu reign in the Qing Dynasty, Britain coveted it and designated Chongqing as a commercial port in the Sino-British Beijing Supplementary Treaty. To this day, various countries' consulates stand in Consulate Lane, their gates half-closed, and the courtyards inside are quiet and secluded, making people feel even more strongly the "open door of the Yangtze River." Since the beginning of the Republic of China, almost all of the more than 470 large and small civil wars in Sichuan Province have centered on the struggle for Chengdu and Chongqing. The importance of Chongqing's position is no less than that of Chengdu.

Since the Central Army entered Sichuan this spring, Chongqing's position has become even more important. Transportation construction has taken Chongqing as its hub, and the economic development of Sichuan will also take Chongqing as its starting point. Recently, the provisional headquarters moved to Chongqing, and the Wuchang provisional headquarters also merged with the Chongqing provisional headquarters. As a result, Chongqing has become the center of national military command. During my stay in Chongqing this time, I spent ten days and saw that the various situations in Chongqing were quite different from those in the downstream ports. I will briefly describe my feelings as follows: 1. Developed Banks and Bankrupt Qianzhuang: Banks were established in Chongqing in the late Qing Dynasty, and after 1930, banking business developed even more rapidly. Although the chaos of Sichuan's finances and the complexity of the monetary system hindered the development of banking business to some extent, banks still showed a growing trend in this state of being riddled with problems. There are two main reasons for this: (1) The continuous collapse of the countryside led to the concentration of bureaucratic and merchant capital in banks; (2) Banks were more convenient than qianzhuang in operating in Shanghai exchange speculation, government bond trading, and interest rate and ocean freight business. For these reasons, except for two or three banks in Chongqing that lost money due to reckless speculation in Shanghai exchange, the rest made huge profits last year. There are now more than a dozen large and small banks in Chongqing, and the branch banks set up by various banks in Chongqing are said to be not included in this number. As for qianzhuang, they have been suppressed by banks, their business is sluggish, and the number has decreased from fifty or sixty to ten or twenty, and there are still more going bankrupt. Since the central government announced the order to recover local banknotes at 80% of their value, a small wave has been stirred up in Chongqing's financial circles. The monetary base has not yet been fully stabilized, and commercial transactions mostly use checks or account transfers. Recently, due to the insufficient supply of central banknotes, there is a 20% discount for exchanging checks for central banknotes, which has caused another disturbance in Chongqing's financial circles, but it does not seem to have much impact on banking business. Recently, the American-Feng Bank in Chongqing has expanded its business, and there is news that the New Industry Bank (formerly an opium industry bank) is being revived. Influenced by Shanghai banks' investment in rural areas, various banks seem to be focusing on rural Sichuan, and as a result, a large number of farmers' banks have been newly established in various counties.

2. Commercial Appearance Still Prosperous: Chongqing's commerce can be roughly divided into categories such as silk, cloth, mountain goods, medicinal materials, salt, sugar, Soviet goods, hardware, cotton yarn, rice, tung oil, tobacco, and shipping. In the past year, the local production of salt and sugar has been sluggish due to the encroachment of foreign goods and the restrictions of taxes and levies. Other grain industries have been profitable due to Shanghai exchange relations or thriving trade. The situation this year is roughly the same as in previous years. Various imported goods are extremely crowded, and the freight rates for upstream ships have risen sharply. Conversely, due to the narrow sales market, the quantity of exported goods is gradually decreasing, but the export of tung oil is still good. According to Mr. Zhou, the manager of the Bank of China, "Oil is a major import, about 8,000 boxes per year. In total, the province's annual trade deficit is about 20 million yuan or more. There is no way to remedy exports, and imports are coming in steadily. If this continues, the situation is very worrying." His words expressed deep emotion. According to my investigation, the Chongqing market is flooded with foreign goods, especially Japanese goods, and the business of various foreign goods stores seems to be particularly developed recently. The wealthy sons and daughters of Chongqing generally like fashion and are good at imitation, specializing in consumption work for foreign merchants. Therefore, the more the city develops, the more the power of foreign merchants increases. The convenience of transportation has created a good opportunity to promote foreign goods, which is quite heartbreaking. Mr. Zhou continued, "Although there is no way to actively increase revenue at present, we should try our best to reduce expenditure. Sichuan has oil everywhere, and Sichuan also has production of cement, gypsum, copper, iron, etc. The raw materials for woolen fabrics are abundant in western and northwestern Sichuan. If raw materials can be fully utilized, outflow can be suppressed and all industries can be developed. The biggest pain in Sichuan now is that there are raw materials but no means of production. How to develop production is the most urgent task."

3. Middlemen Classes Are Quite Overbearing: The middleman class refers to the so-called middlemen, who rely solely on extracting commissions from hard labor for a living. This kind of people occupies a considerable force in Chongqing. Their exploitation of general workers can be described as meticulous. For example, among the organizations of boatmen on ships, rickshaw pullers, wooden boats (small sailboats that Sichuanese call wooden boats), sedan chair carriers (simpler sedan chairs), and dock porters (all manipulated by middlemen), it is not easy for general workers to find work without going through middlemen. And general middlemen often attract many unemployed farmers to flock to the cities in order to exploit them further. The life of general workers is unspeakably miserable. Taking rickshaws as an example, before the Communist bandits fled, the daily rickshaw rent was about 13 diao (each diao is equivalent to more than four cents of silver yuan), plus commission. After paying the rent, the rickshaw pullers had little left, and some even did not earn enough to pay the rent. Later, due to the growing Communist disaster, the municipal authorities reduced the rickshaw rent from 13 diao to 5 diao. It is heard that the Chongqing municipal government is also paying attention to this and will strictly limit this kind of evil habit of extracting labor. If it can be thoroughly handled, the labor community will benefit greatly.

A Distant View of Chongqing City

Random Chat About Rural Life

Casual Talk on the Lives of Farmers in Northern Wuxi 54

— Compiled by Yu Qingtang, Weng Zushan

1. Farmers in the Eyes of Poets

"She cooks under the stove,

Freshly cut mountain firewood

Crackles and pops.

The bright red light in the stove door,

Flashes on her bright red face,

Flashes red on her blue cloth clothes.

He, with a ten-year-old pipe in his mouth,

Slowly returns from the field,

Hangs the hoe in the corner of the house,

And sits on the rice bed,

Teasing the dog of his loved ones.

He also walks to the pen,

To take a look at his ox;

Turns his head and says to her;

"How is it—

Our newly brewed wine?"

"..."

——Liu Bannong, "The Evening of a Small Farming Family"——

In the eyes of poets, the countryside is such a beautiful and fascinating picture! Similarly, when Mr. Yu Dafu toured the famous scenic spots of Zhejiang Province, he also had a short poem describing the scenery of the mountain village. I don't remember the original poem very well, but it seems that the last two sentences were "Children go to pick tea in pairs, and idle away before the bucket with a tree of flowers!" In the poet's pen, the lonely and desolate countryside has become a peaceful world that "is not surprised by knives or soap."

However, we don't have to go to the collection of so-called pastoral poets to find materials. We have to observe and find problems from the real lives of farmers. It turns out that the so-called "poets" are used to using their own joys and sorrows to "illuminate" everything. Below, I will briefly talk about what I have seen about the lives of farmers in the countryside in the past two years.

2. The Farmers I Saw

Here, I can tell the reader a few facts about the countryside:

Once, a simple clinic we ran came to a farmer in her fifties who wanted treatment for her son, who had been suffering from malaria for two years. After she found out that she had to take quinine, she wanted a packet: as usual, she had to be charged six copper coins—because there are many addicts locally, and it costs more than ten yuan a month to cope, so she had to charge a fee—she dug around in her chest for a long time, and unexpectedly dug out an egg. It turned out that the only thing her family could exchange was this only egg! And the one laid yesterday had already been exchanged for kerosene at the grocery store!

I remember when I was at home, I always bought straw in loads of two loads. I have never seen a farmer in the market bringing a bundle of straw to sell, but one day a farmer actually brought a bundle of straw to sell. When asked why he only brought one bundle, his answer was really out of my expectation. "Today, × village pays homage to the gods, and a few copper coins are enough to buy incense and candles." It turns out that the countryside does not need currency much. The flour they eat is just exchanged for wheat—one liter for one liter, which is very fair.

Coming back from the city, when walking through a certain village lane, I often see two or three farmers surrounding a small square stool for meals. I have a little nearsightedness, and at first I didn't pay attention to what they were eating. I thought it was probably nothing more than tofu, pickles, salted fish, and white rice, and they would never get fresh fish and meat. But once I had a whim, and when they were eating, I walked over to take a look, and it shocked me: although I wouldn't mistake wheat for chives, I had never seen what they were eating, of course it was not rice, nor was it porridge, it looked like rice noodles, and like paste. The dishes were just a bowl of broad beans boiled in salt water. It is said that because salt is expensive, there is not much pickled vegetables to eat.

In summer, a rickety old man brought a fourteen or fifteen-year-old child to see a doctor. The old man sat down and was still panting, and the child suddenly fainted! In a hurry, I quickly gave him ammonia to smell, and he slowly woke up. I asked and learned that he had gotten up early today to help his father carry a load of vegetables to the village to sell. He was hungry and wanted to buy two copper coins worth of sweet potatoes, but he had no money. He was sick, walked five or six miles on an empty stomach, and carried vegetables, so naturally he couldn't hold on!

Universal poverty, universally struggling on the line of death! However, these are just the surface appearances in the eyes of outsiders, and they are still just superficial. To know what kind of life they—the farmers—are actually living, it is best to listen to their own complaints. 3. Farmers' Own Words

They were originally "planting fields to eat," but now they universally feel that "there is no benefit in planting fields, and there is no food to eat without planting."

They are most afraid of famine years. A graduate of the senior class of a people's school once wrote such a poem:

"The year is barren, no food to eat!

Sell the old ox, exchange for rice grains.

In the blink of an eye, rice seedlings have to be planted and the soil turned,

Without the old ox, only the plow is left!"

The person who wrote this song is a diligent young farmer, and he is only about twenty years old this year. I believe that when he wrote it, he must have been holding back tears!

But there are even worse things than famine years! Last year's drought caused many farmland to have no harvest. The number of mu of barren land exempted from grain is determined by the government, but farmers cannot enjoy the right to exempt from grain. There is a saying in the countryside called "Barren Years Familiar Books." It turns out that when there is a disaster, there is always land that is exempted from grain. The lower-level clerks who collect grain taxes can fraudulently report barren land as fertile land. Those who plant their own land pay to buy a "barren certificate" to be exempt from grain, and those who plant rented land buy a barren certificate to be exempt from rent; who cares if there is a harvest in your field! Below is a page from the diary of Yu Hongshan, a member of the cooperative: "This morning, I met a worried-looking person, staring blankly at the head of the field. I asked him, and he said, "My family has eight people, planting five mu of land. Unfortunately, this year there was a drought and insect damage, and there was no harvest! Now, not only is there no food or clothing, but there is no way to pay the barren land fee. Without a barren certificate, I have to pay the rent rice, and it seems that there is only one way to die!" I said, "Recently, a notice was posted at the entrance of the ×× township office, stating that all completely barren land can be exempted from grain, and barren land officials are not allowed to charge a single penny. Why are you charging money now?" "Ah, don't say a notice, even if you post a hundred notices, it's useless... They are all in the same gang. At first, the grain clerk and the district clerk took the lead in collecting the fee, charging four corners per mu of barren land before issuing a barren certificate. Later, the chief of the village saw that they were jealous and said to everyone: The grain clerk and the district clerk privately made barren certificates, which are completely invalid and must be issued by the township office to be effective. After that, it was collected by the township office. However, Mr. × said that it was too unpleasant for the township office to collect barren land fees. Therefore, it was moved to ××li to collect. The district clerk got 50 yuan alone, and the rest was divided equally into five shares: the grain clerk, the southern village chief, the northern village chief, the relief association, and the township deputy each got a share. However, those who are barren are really suffering, where can they get the money to get a barren certificate?"

After listening, I couldn't help but stare blankly at the head of the field.

"What if there is no disaster?"

Good harvest, good harvest!

This year I will harvest a few more loads of rice than last year.

Mom laughs haha, little sister jumps with both feet;

'I'm going to make me a new cotton-padded jacket this year.'

'Okay, okay, okay!' A burst of laughter!

Good harvest, good harvest!

The price of rice is really bad, not as high as last year;

The old rent cannot be paid, how dare you delay the cotton-padded jacket?

Winter is coming, winter is coming! Little sister is freezing and crying."

Zhou Shenqing (Graduate of the Senior Class of a People's School)

Now, the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are strictly pursuing old debts of grain tax, aren't they? Grain tax is the main income of the national treasury, and the people have the obligation to pay taxes: if there is a disaster, it can be generously exempted, and if there are old debts, of course, they must be "strictly recovered." But we have to ask, who owes the grain tax? To answer bluntly, all self-cultivating farmers or semi-self-cultivating farmers who go to the fields barefoot have not owed the government half a copper coin! On the contrary, the amount they pay each year exceeds more than double the amount they should pay on the string ticket! Farmers cannot pay grain directly to the grain counter, they can only let the "village chiefs" and local bullies pay on their behalf, and extort money from it. Let's look at the diary of Jin Yun, a student of the People's School:

"A slight breeze brought the sound of coughing, it turned out that Uncle × was also resting under the tree. He continued: "The day before yesterday was the deadline for paying the grain tax from last year. I pawned more than five yuan for the pawn in the bride's room, especially to rush to the city to pay, but I didn't know that the gentleman at the counter checked and said that it had already been paid. As soon as I heard this, I knew that the village chief who paid the grain tax had taken a fancy to me, and I couldn't escape the money! So I went hungry and hurried back to the countryside, and found × village chief in the teahouse in West Street. I said with a smile: Thank you, sir, for paying my grain tax for me, please calculate how much it is? He slowly took out the string ticket and looked at it and said.. According to the string, it costs eleven yuan to pay, plus one yuan for my expenses, a total of twelve yuan. Oh! Old nephew! I should only pay five yuan and forty-five cents, he wants me to pay twelve yuan... more than five yuan, or the pawn in the bride's tears... where is there another six or seven yuan?... Later I said a lot of pleading words to him, but it was still useless. Yesterday I borrowed seven yuan from ×× at a monthly interest rate of five points before it was settled!... Talking about the truth, the old man lowered his head and choked up! I couldn't bear to listen any longer, so I advised him not to cry and go to pick river mud together. I thought that the village chief who eats five liters of rice per mu of farmland from the farmers should always show compassion for our poor people. Who knows that he colluded with the township chief and did all kinds of evil, and even took the opportunity to extort money on the national grain tax. With such insatiable greed, even if we shed all our sweat and blood, working like cattle and horses all year round, we still can't afford to support them...!'"

The "net of heaven and earth" woven by floods, droughts, local bullies, and police officers has tied the farmers so that they cannot move. Their hard work all year round cannot even afford them a full meal. But if they don't plant fields, what else can they do? No wonder they want to make unjust complaints:

"Farmers are busy, farmers are busy,

Farmers are really busy!

The millet is old, harvest the rice;

The rice is on the threshing ground, plant the wheat;

Plant good wheat, grind and thresh;

Grind good threshing, white rice is given to the rich!

Busy all year round,

Hungry and cold!"

—Hua Yimin (Graduate of the Senior Class of a People's School)—

Describing the countryside as a paradise where people are idle is of course a poet's illusion; we can join the farmers' team, or we can recognize a part of their lives; but it is always better to ask them to tell us themselves to be more real and kind! There is a saying: "If the morning man does not plant fields, the city god will cut off the fire, if the farmer does not read books, there is no place to complain." How to make the farmers cry out their own pain?

24, 10, 15, Written in Fengxiang, Wuxi.

Page 8

Local News

Various Circles in Shanghai Held a Memorial Meeting for the Anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Birthday Yesterday 55

More than 300 representatives attended the Municipal People's Education Center. All agencies, etc., flew flags and closed for the holiday. Military police were on alert.

November 12 is the birthday of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the leader of the Chinese Kuomintang. The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters convened representatives from all walks of life at the Municipal People's Education Center on Wenmiao Road at 10:00 a.m. to hold a memorial meeting for the anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's birth. The Chairman of the Municipal Committee, Huang Zaoxiong, reported on the significance of the memorial, and Cai Bubai, the representative of the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, delivered a speech. All agencies, schools, and factories in the city were closed for one day, and all circles flew flags to celebrate. The military and police authorities were also on strict alert. The situation of the memorial meeting is recorded in detail below.

Attending Representatives

Those who attended the memorial meeting included Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Committee, Shi Weijun of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Tan Gengxin of the Audit Office, the Shanghai South Office of the Health Bureau, Qi Shugong, Li Yuanfu of the Fifth District Cigarette Industry Association, Zhu Shengying of the Air Defense Association, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Shi Yuemen of the Jiangxi Fellow Association in Shanghai, Hu Tianseng of the New Movement Association, Yu Yaoqiu of the Baoshan Fellow Association, Cen Chiyao of the Shipping Industry Association, Chang Daotong of the French Concession Taxpayer Association, Hong Hao of the Poor Children's Education Institute, Cai Bubai of the Anti-Smoking Committee, Zhu Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Wu Ding of the Gao Er Branch, Lin Kecong of the Women's Association, Lou Zhaoding of the Navigation Administration, staff members of the Municipal Party Headquarters, representatives of various schools, groups, and party headquarters at all levels, and others, totaling more than 300 people.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremony, the Chairman, Huang Zaoxiong, reported that the birth of Dr. Sun Yat-sen of our party marked the beginning of a new life for the Chinese nation. Dr. Sun Yat-sen created the great Three Principles of the People in his doctrine and organized the revolutionary Kuomintang in his career, enabling the Chinese nation to break away from the shackles of autocracy and embark on the open road of freedom and equality. Therefore, when we commemorate Dr. Sun Yat-sen, in addition to expressing our admiration for Dr. Sun Yat-sen's great revolutionary cause, we should also earnestly abide by and strive for the teachings that Dr. Sun Yat-sen left us. Among Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, the most unforgettable for us are "peace," "struggle," and "saving China." Because to unite domestically, strengthen national power, obtain freedom and equality from our own national status, and then achieve the goal of world harmony, we must start with "peace." Because to advance all undertakings in China and overcome all difficulties, we must also struggle. Being able to "peace" and being able to "struggle" can "save China." Furthermore, the fearless spirit shown in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's lifelong career should be emulated even more when the national crisis is becoming increasingly serious today. These are a few things I wanted to say today. Over.

Mr. Cai's Speech

Then, Cai Bubai, the representative of the Anti-Smoking Committee, delivered a speech, stating briefly that today I would like to take this opportunity to report to you on some matters related to anti-smoking. The degree to which the prevalence of opium in China harms the country and the nation is already clear to everyone. But why does opium have such a deep-rooted force in China? After so many anti-smoking campaigns, why hasn't there been a very good result? It can be roughly divided into three reasons: (1) The reason of national character, because of the laziness and conservatism of the Chinese nation, an inextricable relationship occurred after opium was imported; (2) The reason of politics, because of the restrictions of unequal treaties and the desire of warlords and corrupt officials to seek personal gain, opium was able to circulate freely in the country; (3) The reason of society, because general traitors tried to make huge profits and the environment was bad, causing the spread of opium. We must start from three aspects in the future to carry out anti-smoking: (1) Sanctions by public opinion; (2) Sanctions by politics; (3) Improving the environment. Now the government has made the greatest determination to strictly prohibit opium. I hope that all of you present can assist the government in implementing the anti-smoking policy.

Memorial Slogans

(1) To commemorate the leader, we must eliminate the Red bandits and appease the refugees. (2) Work hard and implement the resolutions of the Fifth National Congress. (3) Gather the will of the entire party and strengthen the power of the country. (4) Unite sincerely and support the Fifth National Congress. (5) The anniversary of the leader's birth is the memorial day for the development of a new life for the Chinese nation. (6) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang. (7) Long live the Three Principles of the People. (8) Long live the Republic of China.

Municipal Government Memorial

Yesterday (the 12th) was the anniversary of the leader's birth. All the staff of the municipal government gathered in the auditorium of the municipal central district at 10:00 a.m. to hold a memorial ceremony. Because Mayor Wu went to Beijing to attend a meeting, Secretary-General Yu presided over the meeting and led the ceremony. He then reported on the significance of the memorial and encouraged his colleagues to continue the leader's legacy, work together with one heart and one mind, and complete the leader's great revolutionary cause, etc.

Memorial by Party Headquarters on Both Railways

Yesterday was the 70th anniversary of the leader's birth. The Special Party Headquarters of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways held a memorial meeting at the headquarters. More than 100 people who signed in were the entire staff of the headquarters, as well as representatives of the railway bureau, various schools, employees, and groups. Chairman Li Dasan presided over the ceremony and then reported on the significance of commemorating the leader's birth and celebrating the Fifth National Congress. Then, representatives of the railway bureau, Fan Shouzhu, and employees Yang Youren, Li Guohua, Zhang Yunhe, and other comrades delivered speeches. They then shouted slogans and adjourned the meeting.

Zou Lu Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon from Guangdong 56

Accompanied Guan Suiren and Others to Nanjing to Attend the Fifth Plenary Session

Central Executive Committee member Zou Lu, who departed from Hong Kong on the Pacific Steamship Company's General Pershing liner on the 9th to travel north, was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 8 a.m. yesterday. However, due to fog encountered en route, the ship's progress was slower, and it did not enter the Wusongkou until noon yesterday. It docked at the China Merchants Bureau's North Bund Wharf at that time. Those who came to welcome him included Kong Xiangxi, Song Ziwen, Xu Kan, and other representatives, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Hai'an, Deputy Finance Minister Zou Lin, Vice President of the Judicial Yuan Qin Zhen, Central Executive Committee member Huang Jilu, Guan Suiren, Cui Guangxi, Li Renren, Deng Qingyang, Yang Dezhao, Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission member Xie Zhongfu, Shanghai Municipal Government representative Li Dachao, Municipal Security Bureau representative Wang Zhinan, Municipal Party Headquarters representative Tong Xingbai, and over sixty of Zou's friends.

Proceeding to Nanjing That Evening

After the ship docked, all the welcoming personnel boarded the ship to greet him. They then disembarked and went directly to the Cangzhou Hotel to rest. In the evening, they attended a banquet hosted by friends in Shanghai. Afterward, at 11 p.m., they took the night express train to Nanjing. Central Executive Committee members Guan Suiren, Huang Jilu, Li Renren, Cui Guangxi, Deng Qingyang, Liu Luyin, Zhan Jusi, Bai Wenwei, He Shizhen, Yunnan representatives Zhang Xilin, Pei Cunfan, Lu Zian, and others traveled to Nanjing on the same train to attend this morning's Fifth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang.

Zou's Remarks

Zou looked energetic, although his face appeared somewhat older than before. According to his written statement issued upon arrival in Shanghai, "This time, because comrades from all parties at the Fifth National Congress felt the country's plight was increasingly urgent and there should be a method of uniting to save the nation, and because the Central Government repeatedly requested comrades Dai Jitao and Ma Chaojun to come south to urge us, all the Central Executive Committee members from the Southwest, except those who were ill or had special duties, have come to Nanjing to attend. Those who came before me included Liu Luyin, Li Renren, Huang Jilu, Deng Qingyang, Cui Guangxi, Zhan Jusi, and other committee members. Those who came separately from me include Lin Yunhai, Huang Xuchu, Chen Yaoyuan, Chen Jiayou, Xiong Kewu, Liu Jiwen, and other committee members. In addition, there are dozens of representatives from Guangdong and Guangxi and overseas, as well as university professor Dr. Cao Siwu, etc. My personal advocacy is to follow the consistent aim of saving the country, seeking national unity to overcome the national crisis. Therefore, in this time of serious national crisis, all who save the country are comrades, and all who do not save the country are enemies. This attendance at the Fifth National Congress is based on this aim, to earnestly discuss with all comrades how to start with our party to save the current crisis of the party and the nation. The current situation in China is full of holes, such as politics, diplomacy, finance, economy, military affairs, rural areas, business circles, industry, disaster relief, etc. All need to work hard to improve and rescue. If our party can first adhere to the aim of saving the country, unite as one, and then, based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's heart that the world is for all, put it into practice, and the entire party and nation take responsibility together, I believe that although China is in danger, there are still ways to solve the problems, which is what I deeply believe. The 11th of this month is the 11th anniversary of Sun Yat-sen University, and the ceremony for moving five colleges of the university to the new campus will also be held (Sun Yat-sen University has six colleges: Literature, Law, Science, Engineering, Agriculture, and Medicine. Except for the medical college, which needs to be close to the city and will not be moved, the other five colleges have all moved to the new campus in Shipai). I have many personal matters, but because this Fifth National Congress is of great importance, I cannot but spare the time to attend. As for the new campus of Sun Yat-sen University in Shipai, construction began in March 1933 and was completed last year. There is a bronze statue of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, an agricultural museum of the agricultural college, several sericulture museums, several rice cultivation fields, a chemistry museum of the science college, an electrical and mechanical engineering classroom of the engineering college, a civil engineering classroom, six male dormitories, and one female dormitory. Therefore, in the autumn of last year, the three colleges of Agriculture, Engineering, and Law were moved to the new campus. Because the classrooms of the science college were not enough, the law college was moved instead. Completed this year are a southern gate archway, a western gate stone archway, the entire literature college, the entire law college, a biology, geography, and geology classroom of the science college, a mathematics, astronomy, and physics classroom, a chemical engineering classroom of the engineering college, a materials testing laboratory, a weak current testing laboratory, two factories, two agricultural and forestry chemistry museums of the agricultural college, an agricultural mat manufacturing room, two greenhouses, an agricultural field office, a forest office, an agricultural tool room, a storage room, each one, a power plant, several water storage fields, pumping rooms, and ancillary buildings, a water tower filtration room and ancillary buildings, a large faculty dormitory, three male dormitories, one female dormitory, a temporary hospital, a dozen sports fields and ball fields, a male swimming pool and a female swimming pool each, a milk room, cow house, pigsty, and chicken farm each. This autumn, the two colleges of Literature and Science will also be moved to the new campus in Shipai. From this point on, all five colleges of the university will be moved. From the start of construction to August of this year, it took 30 months, with a total construction cost of approximately 5 million yuan. The faculty dormitory can accommodate more than 200 people, and the male and female dormitories can accommodate more than 2,000 people. The entire campus covers more than 12,000 mu, with approximately 100 li of roads already built, and a total of more than 4.5 million trees have been planted in the agricultural fields and forests. This is the only university personally founded by Dr. Sun Yat-sen and the only university of our party to commemorate Dr. Sun Yat-sen. The current situation can be told in passing."

Sino-French Air Transport Joint Venture Preparing to Launch Next Spring 58

Divided into Two Routes to the Exchange Station in Annam

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Sino-Aviation Company and the French side are conducting a Sino-French joint air transport venture. This matter has been negotiated several times by both parties and has become a reality. It is now scheduled to be completed within this year and officially launched in January next year. According to the news from the Sino-Aviation Company in this port yesterday, the joint transport contract between China and France has been officially signed. The route has been determined to be two lines, one from Guangzhou in Guangdong directly to Annam, and the other from Yunnan to Annam. Both lines use Annam as a joint transport exchange station. Whether the aircraft flying on the two lines will be Douglas aircraft or newly purchased Junkers aircraft is still undecided. In addition, the weekly flight dates and frequencies will be discussed later.

Eurasia's Second Giant Aircraft Took Maiden Voyage on the Shaanxi-Sichuan Line Yesterday 59

Carrying Five Passengers from Various Places

The Ministry of Communications' Eurasia Aviation Corporation leased a second giant aircraft from Germany. It took off from Longhua Airport at 6:30 yesterday morning and took its maiden voyage west on the Shaanxi-Sichuan line, carrying five passengers from various places and a large number of mails from Zhengzhou, Xi'an, Chengdu, and other places. In the afternoon, according to the company's spokesperson speaking to the Hua Dong News Agency reporter, the aircraft had passed Xi'an at 1 p.m. and continued to fly to Chengdu.

To Conduct Earnest Consultations with the Banking Syndicate to Ensure Success

Xu Qingfu, Director of the Finance Department of Zhejiang Province, specially sent a letter to Zhang Shenzhi, a Standing Committee member of the Ningbo Shanghai Compatriots Association, yesterday regarding the fishermen's loan, asking him to conduct earnest consultations with the banking syndicate to save the fishermen from their predicament. The original letter stated, "Mr. Shenzhi, Greetings, This is to inform you that Dinghai's fishing industry has always been prosperous. Recently, due to the tightening policy of financial institutions, fishing warehouses have difficulty in turnover and cannot lend, causing fishermen to be unable to set sail, and the livelihood of fishermen is extremely worrying. Our department previously convened a meeting to discuss with the Central, China, Communications, Siming, China Real Estate Zhejiang, and other banks to each lend 50,000 yuan to organize cooperatives to lend to fishermen for rescue. The Bank of China has agreed because it is a production loan, but on the condition that it cooperates with other banks, but the Siming and other banks have not agreed, and there is still no agreement. I dare to ask you to appeal on your behalf to Zhuotang Mengjia and other fellow villagers in the vicinity to ensure success. The Bank of Communications has been established in Dinghai for many years and has a deep history, and it is heard that it receives a lot of deposits. Please discuss earnestly with Mr. Yigu and join the lending group together. I am dealing with the implementation of the legal tender and have to deal with many matters, so I cannot come to Shanghai in person. I specially instructed Zhang Danren to pay a visit. I have long admired your service and your contribution to your hometown. You will surely receive strong assistance. Mr. Zhang is deeply aware of the situation of the fishing industry in Dingyi. If you have any questions, please consult him face to face. This is specially to inform you and wish you well, Your younger brother Xu Qingfu. It is now known that Zhang has decided to consult with the banking community within days after receiving the letter."

Saving Disaster Victims Is Saving Lives

Donate One More Coin, Save One More Life

Agricultural Chemical Manufacturing Plant Sells Soy Sauce with a Percentage to Help Relief 68

Ms. Mengzhang Performs in Drama, Ticket Sales Are Surprisingly Successful

The various provincial flood relief associations in this city believe that the flood disaster in various places this year is extremely serious, more than ever before. Moreover, the winter cold has arrived, and the north wind is roaring. The hunger and cold are pressing, and even if they do not starve to death, they will freeze to death. Therefore, the relief work cannot be delayed for a moment. The flood relief association has been appealing to all parties for donations on behalf of the disaster victims and has successively held various recreational activities to use all the income for relief. Since the beginning of the fundraising, fortunately, all parties have enthusiastically supported and assisted, and the effectiveness has been satisfactory. Recently, the water disaster general donation and the Boy Scout general mobilization fundraising were also held. The two-day external fundraising has ended, and the results are also very good. According to the Boy Scout directors and members in charge, the number of external donations has not yet been fully submitted by each team, and it will probably be announced soon. The Boy Scouts from each team are now soliciting donations from their relatives and friends. All parties are also moved by the Boy Scouts' lively innocence and tactful statements, and they are even more aware of the misery of the disaster victims, so they are happy to donate. The factory owners Shen Yanghou, Pu, and Cao of the China Agricultural Chemical Manufacturing Plant in this city, in view of the above situation, believe that all Chinese people should do their best to donate to provide relief. The factory, in order to be pragmatic, will reduce the original price of 30,000 bottles of the factory's "Three Fresh" soy sauce and sell them, using one-third of the proceeds to relieve the disaster victims. Donors can provide relief to the disaster victims and also get practical benefits, which is a win-win situation. Soy sauce is a daily necessity for every household, and it must be manufactured using scientific methods to eliminate preservatives. The factory is guided by this principle to manufacture it. This is beneficial to others and self, which is very good. It is heard that this plan has been negotiated by the factory manager Shen with the deputy director of the fundraising group of the Flood Relief Association, Li Dachao, and is now asking the Shanghai Boy Scout Council to entrust the Boy Scout teams in this city to help sell it during this internal fundraising. We hope that all sectors will enthusiastically contribute to this good deed, and the merit is immeasurable. As for the money from the sales, in addition to being received by the Boy Scouts who sell it, the rest can be sent to the temporary office of the fundraising group of the Flood Relief Association on the third floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA, and the goods will be delivered to the address at any time. In addition, Ms. Meng Xiaodong and Ms. Zhang Eyun will perform dramas at the Golden Theater at the invitation of the Flood Relief Association to help relief. They have already taken the stage yesterday, and the ticket sales are surprisingly successful, which is beyond our expectations. After 8 o'clock, the "Sold Out" sign was hung up at the theater, which shows that Ms. Meng and Ms. Zhang's theatrical skills and calling ability are very large. If people from all walks of life who are enthusiastic about disaster relief want to order tickets, they should do so as soon as possible to avoid missing out.

Vietnamese Overseas Chinese Tycoon Yan Zijun and Others Organize Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association 71

According to the Shanghai Times News Agency, according to news from the overseas Chinese agency in this city, Vietnamese overseas Chinese tycoons Yan Zijun, Lei Jianqing, and others, in view of the lack of prosperity in the motherland's industry, have contacted overseas Chinese from various places to organize the Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association. The outline for preparation has also been drafted, and a declaration has been issued to respectfully inform domestic compatriots. The general idea of the declaration is to concentrate financial resources and recruit talents to operate the motherland's industry in a scientific way, on the one hand, to seek development for the motherland, and on the other hand, to seek a way out for overseas Chinese. Its effectiveness is more practical than any other way to save the country. The outline for the preparation of the association is recorded below: Outline of the Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association, Article 1, The name of this association is the Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association, Article 2, This association is based on the need to save the country and save ourselves, to unite overseas Chinese in various ports to revitalize the motherland's industry as its purpose, Article 3, The tasks of this association are as follows: (1) Please ask the central and provincial industrial agencies or schools and groups to send all specific plans for industry to this association for selection. (2) Contact various specialized technical personnel to organize various industrial research associations in order to formulate investigation methods and review various industrial plans for development. (3) For all kinds of beneficial industries that this association decides to develop, contact various ports to raise capital separately. After the capital is raised, this association will convene a shareholders' meeting and transfer the business to the company for management. (4) The company that this association sponsors has the obligation of guidance, auditing, and supervision. (5) The expenses before the establishment of the company shall be borne by the company. Article 4, The organizational outline of this association is as follows: 1. Important commercial ports in various parts of Southeast Asia each organize a certain local Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association as the basic group of this association. 2. Each association selects several representatives to organize the Overseas Chinese Industry Promotion Association.

Red Swastika Society: Report on the Tragic Situation in the Zhongxiang Disaster Area 72

President Han Fuhang Returns to Shanghai to Report

This newspaper has repeatedly reported that the Red Swastika Society previously appointed Presidents Han Fuhang and Li Yizhen to lead a relief team, carrying a large quantity of medicines and burial equipment, to Hubei Province to oversee the Yangtze River flood relief efforts. It is now known that President Han returned to Shanghai on the 6th of this month after inspecting the disaster areas. According to him, since arriving in Hubei, he has intensified the supervision and implementation of relief work, and reallocated the relief funds after inspecting the disaster areas. However, the disaster situation in Hubei Province this time is truly unprecedented and extremely tragic. The most severely affected areas include Hanyang, Hanchuan, Zhongxiang, and Tianmen counties, where floodwaters have not yet receded, leaving behind a vast expanse of water. Hanyang and Hanchuan have already been investigated and relief distributed once, and teams are now being sent to continue the relief work. Tianmen has already completed the relief distribution organized by benevolent individuals. However, after inspecting Zhongxiang County, the tragic situation there is truly beyond description. The county covers a vast area, with an east-west diameter of 190 li and a similar north-south extent. The county is divided into ten districts, with Districts 1, 2, 6, and 9 being the most severely affected. When the floodwaters suddenly descended, the water level reached approximately 40 chi, engulfing the city. This resulted in the drowning of over 23,000 people, with over 320,000 people affected. Homes, fields, graves, grain, and tools were all washed away. Over 700,000 mu of farmland were submerged, 200,000 mu were covered in sand, and over 50,000 houses were destroyed. Along the way, rubble was everywhere, and piles of white bones were seen. The landscape was entirely desert-like, resembling a living hell. At night, the cries of the disaster victims embracing each other could be heard from several li away, a truly unbearable sound. Although the Swastika Society, in conjunction with the Chinese and foreign benevolent relief organizations and the Hubei Benevolent Relief Office, has allocated 40,000 yuan for emergency relief, this amount is definitely insufficient to address the severity of the disaster. Furthermore, the county is 800 li by water and over 600 li by land from Hankou, and the road for motor vehicles has been washed away, making it extremely difficult to transport grain. A second relief team has now been dispatched to conduct further investigations. There are still many counties awaiting relief. It is hoped that benevolent people from all walks of life will have great compassion, generously open their purses, and contribute to this righteous cause. Even donating one gold coin can save a life, bringing immeasurable merit. We cannot help but appeal on behalf of the disaster victims.

Municipal Federation Notifies All Branches to Strictly Prevent Merchants from Buying Silver Coins; Any Discovery Should Be Immediately Reported to the Police for Investigation 75

According to Dagongshe, the Municipal Federation of Citizens of the First Special District believes that the government's resolute reform of the currency system this time is sincerely supported by the people of the country. However, a small number of unscrupulous merchants and vagrants are being used by others, disregarding the law, and secretly buying silver at high prices. The federation issued a special notice to all district branches yesterday, emphasizing the importance of complying with the law. If any of the above-mentioned situations occur, they should immediately report to the local police authorities for arrest and strict handling, in order to warn against illegal activities. The original text reads: "Regarding the urgent notice, since our country has been affected by the drastic changes in world silver prices, silver outflows, and currency contraction, the industrial and commercial sectors have been declining daily, and the social economy has developed into an unstable state. Our central authorities, in order to save the national economy and stabilize society, announced on the 4th of this month that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications will be used as legal tender, reversing the tide and benefiting the country and the people. However, it has been reported that in the Hongkou district and other areas, small money shops and small cigarette paper shops, etc., are being used by others and are willing to flout the law and secretly buy silver coins, which is truly hateful. (It has now been resolved by the sixth executive committee meeting of this federation to notify all district branches to convey this to their member stores, and to pay close attention. If any of the above-mentioned situations are discovered again, the traitor should be immediately reported to the police for investigation, in order to block the outflow of silver, and to ensure the foundation of the country and society. This matter concerns the foundation of the nation, and it is hoped that everyone will follow and handle it accordingly. This special notice is hereby given."

Three Vagrants Sent to the Xi Qin Institute 80

Liu Lingfang, the chief of the Yemiao Police Station, was patrolling the area at 7:10 PM yesterday when he noticed a person near the Yemiao wearing a padded jacket and an overcoat, resembling a vagrant. This reminded him of the frequent incidents of extortion in the area, so he immediately ordered the person to stop for questioning. However, the person was evasive, so he ordered the constable Zhang Chenghua to take him to the station. He also found a person in the Yemiao wearing old underwear and a leather overcoat, looking suspicious, and found a counterfeit yuan of foreign currency on him. At the same time, another person was also taken to the station by constable Chen Zhaolin for dressing inappropriately and looking like a vagrant. After Chief Liu returned to the station, he interrogated the accused, who identified himself as Lu Guoliang, 31 years old, from Changzhou, a comb maker, living at No. 47 Xue Longdi. He ordered the sergeant Li Hongqing to investigate in detail and found that Lu had been making combs several years ago, but now specializes in extortion. It was also found that the other two people, Gu Yuqing and Tian Chunshan, were local vagrants with no permanent occupation, engaged in extortion. Chief Liu believed that these vagrants, who do not engage in production, must be up to no good. As the winter defense period is approaching, if they are not sent to the bureau for investigation, it would be insufficient to maintain local security. He ordered them to be sent to the Municipal Police Headquarters for transfer to the Xi Qin Institute for rehabilitation.

Zhao Anzhi Holds Painting Exhibition in Beijing 81

Zhao Anzhi, a painter from Wujin, held a public exhibition at the First Park in Beijing, causing a sensation throughout the city. Thousands of visitors from all walks of life came to see the exhibition every day. Zhao's paintings are based on the court style of the Song Dynasty, and his use of color is also exquisite. He uses colors such as celadon green, which were common during the Ming and Qing dynasties. His use of color and brushwork echoes the ancients. Zhao has participated in the Belgian World Expo and won a gold medal, as well as participated in the Sino-German Painting Exhibition at the Chicago Expo, where he also received high praise.

Searching for His Wife Unsuccessfully, He Attempted Suicide by Drowning and Was Rescued 82

His family has more than ten mu of land and usually lives by farming. His wife, Zhou, has been working as a servant in the Zhu residence in Ba Xian Fang, Ba Xian Qiao, in the French Concession of Shanghai. He has not heard from her for more than a year. Recently, due to the scarcity in the countryside, he could not make a living, so he borrowed two yuan for travel expenses to Shanghai to look for his wife. Unexpectedly, she had left with someone to Minhang, so he pawned his jacket and took a car to Minhang. After searching for several days, he had no news. Being unfamiliar with the area and penniless, he had not eaten for two days. He walked to the Wu Jiaxiang area, where he was so hungry that he could not continue. Gold Prices Soar, Bread and Other Industries Raise Prices 87

Since the soaring gold prices, imported raw materials have increased in cost due to exchange rates. Therefore, the bread, mirror-making, and camel hair industries have successively issued notices of price increases, which are listed separately below:

Bread

The bread industry association members in this city, including Dongfang, Huili, Wanguo, Dahua, Xingli, Shunquan, Ruita, Hetai, Huitai, Jinxing, and Nanfang, jointly announced price increases: "To our valued customers, due to the rising prices of various goods, the cost of imported raw materials has increased by 30%. In order to maintain capital, our association has decided to post notices of price increases in Shen and Xin newspapers for two days each, starting today, and implement the price increases on the 16th. Based on the old price list, we will increase prices by 25% in order to maintain business operations. We hope that you will understand. Sincerely, Dongfang, Huili, Wanguo, Dahua, Xingli, Shunquan, Ruita, Hetai, Huitai, Jinxing, Nanfang."

Mirror Making

The Mirror Making Industry Association announced: "To our valued customers, our industry published a notice on October 18 to slightly increase prices, and we are grateful for the enthusiastic support of our customers. However, the foreign exchange rate has recently shrunk sharply, and the prices of all raw materials have increased accordingly, resulting in a sharp increase in costs. We have no choice but to find ways to remedy this situation. However, considering the market situation, we cannot suddenly continue to raise prices. The costs of the industry should also be taken into account. Therefore, we specially convened a meeting of industry colleagues to discuss and unanimously decided to temporarily increase prices by 10% based on the prices negotiated on October 18 in order to maintain capital. In addition to sending special letters of notification, we are publishing this public notice again for your consideration."

Camel Hair

(1) Weilun Woolen Mill announced that due to the sharp decline in foreign exchange rates and the skyrocketing prices of materials, the cost has increased. From November 10th, striped camel hair will increase by 2 jiao 5 fen per yard, and plain camel hair will increase by 2 jiao per yard. (2) Tianxiang Camel Hair Factory announced that the competition for wool back and plain camel hair has been fierce in recent years, and the price has been at its lowest limit. Now, due to the soaring prices of raw materials, which far exceed the selling price, prices should be formally increased to maintain capital. However, given the current economic downturn in various industries, we can only slightly increase prices in order to maintain a livelihood. We hope that those who love and use domestic goods will sympathize with us. Thank you for your understanding. (3) Dada Camel Hair Factory announced that all floral and plain items will increase in price: "Recently, due to the sudden decline in foreign exchange rates, the cost of raw materials has increased. If we do not raise the price of our products, it will not be enough to maintain our operations. Therefore, starting today, we will increase the price by 2 jiao per yard. We hope that all the esteemed firms will understand."

The City Was Gloomy Yesterday 89

Low Pressure Passed Through in the Afternoon, Heavy Fog at Night, The Weather Will Turn Cold, and It Will Be Sunny and Good Today

The city experienced a slight rain from 10:00 PM the night before last, which gradually stopped at 10:00 AM yesterday morning. Then, at noon, it was as gloomy as night, and shops, markets, trams, public buses, and roads were illuminated with electric lights to maintain traffic. From 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM, a low-pressure system blew in from the Changsha area, passing through the city between 32 degrees north latitude and 119 degrees east longitude. In the morning, the city experienced a southeast wind, which suddenly turned into a northwest wind. The air pressure was 30.16 at 4:00 AM. The low-pressure system caused heavy fog, and at night, one could not see one's fingers. The mist was especially dense on the Huangpu River. According to astronomical observations, the weather will turn slightly colder within the day, and it will be sunny and good today. Also, the temperature was very warm yesterday, with a minimum of 54.1 degrees and a maximum of 61 degrees.

Rural Woman Dies Tragically After Slipping on a Bamboo Ladder 93

Brain Concussion and Ear Bleeding Lead to Death

Cheng Jishi, a 42-year-old rural woman from Suzhou, had been working as a domestic servant in Shanghai. Recently, she had been unemployed and was staying temporarily at Zhang Lao's employment agency for Yangzhou natives at No. 42 Route du Père Huc in the French Concession, waiting for work. In the evening, she stayed on the loft floor of the employment agency. At 6:00 AM on the 10th, Cheng got up to comb her hair, intending to look for employment. While descending the bamboo ladder, she slipped and fell headfirst from the loft floor, her head hitting the floor. She suffered a brain concussion and profuse bleeding from her ears, immediately losing consciousness. The employment agency reported the incident to the French Concession Police, who immediately summoned an ambulance to take her to Guangci Hospital. Due to the severity of her injuries, medical treatment was ineffective, and she died that night. The hospital notified the police, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. Since she had no family in Shanghai, the next day, Prosecutor Wang Ren of the Special Second Court, accompanied by a forensic doctor and clerk, visited the funeral home. The autopsy confirmed that the deceased had died from a head injury sustained in a fall. The prosecutor questioned the witness, Mrs. Zhang Wang, the owner of the employment agency, about the circumstances of the fall. He then ordered the body to be handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for burial, pending identification by relatives. Subsequently, the employment agency notified her guarantor, who sent someone to Suzhou to urge her husband, Liu Jin'an (48 years old), to come to Shanghai yesterday. According to him, the deceased was indeed Mrs. Liu. Her husband first went to the autopsy room to claim the body for encoffining, and today he will submit a petition to the Special Second Court for permission to transport the coffin back for burial.
