Autopsy Confirms That Woman Zhu Xu Died from Cerebral Hemorrhage 98

Shi Chen Acquitted of Manslaughter

Zhu Xu, a 58-year-old local woman, had previously rented out the remaining rooms of her house at No. 4, Lane 357, Tianjin Road, to Shi Chen, a woman from Huzhou. On the 24th of last month, Zhu demanded three yuan in owed rent from Shi, which led to an argument. As a result, Zhu was pushed down and fell. Two hours later, Zhu suddenly died. Feng Xiushan, a Chinese detective from the Lao Zha Police Station, arrested Shi and sent her to the First Special District Court, charged with manslaughter. However, the medical examination of Zhu Xu determined that her blood pressure was twice as high as normal and that she had died from a cerebral hemorrhage. Therefore, Judge Qian Hongye of the Criminal Division of the First Special Court announced yesterday that Shi Chen was acquitted, and the plaintiff's incidental civil lawsuit was dismissed.

Second Public Utilities Committee: Detailed Discussion on Telephone Rate Increase Proposal 99

Supplementary Report Submitted for Discussion: Final Majority Approval of Experts' Proposals

The Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) Telephone Expert Committee's telephone report was convened for two meetings by the SMC Public Utilities Committee. After detailed discussion and repeated deliberation, the report was approved by the Public Utilities Committee with a majority in favor. During the SMC Board of Directors' special meeting the day before yesterday, the minutes of the Public Utilities Committee meeting were accepted, and the expert report was approved based on the Public Utilities Committee's recommendations. Details were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Upon reviewing the minutes of the Public Utilities Committee's first meeting on the 28th of last month, which were previously published in Chinese and foreign newspapers, the details of the second meeting held on the 7th of this month are disclosed below, selecting the important points:

On this day, the first item the Public Utilities Committee put forward for discussion was the supplementary document added by the experts after the general report. A certain committee member immediately raised a question, stating that according to the experts' supplementary opinion, if the current metered rate system is maintained, the monthly fee for commercial telephones should be increased to $15.50. The original request from the telephone company was only $15.06. Why is the rate proposed by the experts higher than what the company requested? Expert Brown immediately replied that the current situation has undergone substantial changes. The number of telephone sets is expected to decrease by several thousand within this year. This loss should be included in the calculation starting from January 1st of next year. Furthermore, since this year's capital expenditure has increased, the depreciation reserve for the coming year will inevitably be greater than the current one. The committee member then asked if the company's side had been shortsighted and had not foreseen this. Brown replied that the company originally hoped for an increase of 4,000 telephone sets, but now not only is there no increase, but there is also a decrease of 4,000 sets. The difference results in a loss of income equivalent to 8,000 telephone sets for the company. Another committee member then asked why commercial telephones need to be increased more than residential telephones. Brown replied that the current telephone fees paid by residential telephones have long exceeded what they should be paying. If they are increased too much in the future, the development prospects of that type of telephone may be affected. The chairman pointed out that, according to Brown's statement, the company lost 8,000 telephone sets. If each set is rented at $15 per month, the monthly loss would be $120,000, and the annual loss would be $1.44 million. Brown also stated that the 2% annual tax paid by the telephone company to the French Concession SMC and the International Settlement SMC was only paid for part of this year, from August to the end of the year. However, starting next year, it will be paid according to the full year. The committee member said that the company must have known this when requesting the price increase. Therefore, is this decrease in telephone sets due to the metered rate system? Brown replied that the metered rate system is certainly one of the reasons for the decrease in telephone sets. As supplemented in the report, it is stated, "We firmly believe that if this metered rate system continues, the number of telephone sets will inevitably decrease day by day." According to what we have long known, many smaller users are anticipating that the measured service billing system will definitely be implemented, so they have not cancelled their telephones. If the metered rate system is maintained in the future, the decrease in users will inevitably be more severe. As for the exact number of smaller users who have not cancelled their telephones due to anticipating the measured service billing system, according to Brown, it is quite difficult to count. However, roughly speaking, the loss of telephone sets this year is more than half due to the metered rate system. The decrease in telephone sets this year has reached 3,400 sets, and most of those who stopped using the telephone belong to small users. Therefore, it is known that the metered rate system was appropriate in the past, but now the scope of the concession has expanded and the environment has changed.

A certain committee member immediately rose and stated that, according to the report, in 1931, the number of telephone sets increased by 2,996 sets, which is 8% of the total number of telephone sets in 1930. In 1932, it increased by 6,177 sets, which is 16% of the total number in 1931. In 1933, it increased by 4,796 sets, which is 11% of the total number in 1932. In 1934, it increased by 5,460 sets, which is 11% of the total number in 1933. All of these years used the metered rate system, but the number of telephone sets did not decrease due to the disadvantages of the metered rate system. Therefore, the current decrease in telephone sets is more likely due to economic recession. The chairman stated that what has been said above is indeed reasonable, and the reduction of the initial supply cost is urgently needed. Expert Rae stated that the rapid increase in telephone sets in the previous years had two major reasons: first, the development of the telephone business had been suppressed and latent for a long time; and second, after the establishment of the new company, the equipment was changed to automatic, and the telephone business showed a vigorous trend. However, that development will definitely not continue to grow under the metered rate system. Only after the new system is implemented will the telephone business see a resurgence, without any doubt. According to Brown, the total number of telephone sets is currently about 48,000, but from the perspective of the company's equipment scope, this number is not economical. Some committee members asked what number would be economical. Brown replied that, in the telephone business, they have never reached the point of saturation. However, if Shanghai has reached this point, and there is no need to add new equipment or new stations, then on every 10,000-line system, at peak times, it can supply 9,000 telephone sets. However, under the metered rate system, due to the extremely large volume of calls, the central switching station originally had a 10,000-line system, but it could only supply 6,000 telephone sets. If the company's entire equipment capacity can be applied to 80% or 90%, to the point where there is no room for further development, then they can say that they have reached an extremely economical and satisfactory state. Some outsiders say that the company has too many idle equipment, but if the idle equipment is 40%, it would be a mistake to say that it is a 40% waste. Major telephone businesses around the world are constantly reviewing and investigating the status of idle equipment. Taking Shanghai as an example, changes in the situation should also be taken into consideration. For example, residents in the central area are moving to the suburbs, and underground equipment must be increased accordingly. These are all matters that experts constantly consider.

Some committee members asked the experts to compare Shanghai's telephone supply with that of London and New York. Brown said that, according to what he knows and has heard, the supply in this city is not inferior to that of anywhere in the world. However, the humidity in this city is too high, and residents in small streets often hang miscellaneous items on the telephone lines, which the company cannot prohibit. Therefore, the obstacles caused by this may not be few. Rae also said that, according to his experience in using telephones and the information obtained from investigating the company's records, the telephones in Shanghai can indeed be compared with those in New York, Chicago, or elsewhere. Inada said that telephones in Tokyo, Japan, are also often affected by humidity, but not as much as in Shanghai. Other obstacles that Shanghai has, Japan also has. Generally speaking, the telephone supply in Shanghai is not inferior to that in Japan.

A committee member asked why the United States used the metered rate system in various cities 30 or 40 years ago, and then changed to the measured service billing system, but after a short period of time, some cities returned to the metered rate system. Rae replied that from 1895 to 1900, there was a trend in the telephone business to change from metered to measured service. This was a common trend in major cities. He had never heard of a measured service billing system being changed back to a metered rate system. However, in certain areas of New York and Boston, users used to pay by meter, but their calls were limited to a very small number of neighboring users. If they talked to users outside of these few users, they still had to pay 5 cents, 10 cents, or 20 cents for each call. He knew that this was indeed implemented in New York, Boston, and Philadelphia. However, Chicago has always used the measured service billing system. In the aforementioned areas, there were also terms such as "intra-zone" and "intra-city" call fees.

Brown further pointed out that the experts stated in the report that the metered rate system can only be implemented when the user scope does not exceed one switching exchange. If in London, more than 90% of calls need to go through a connection procedure. If all users are within the scope of one switching exchange, the cost of cables between stations can be reduced. If the number of switching stations increases, the cost will have to be multiplied. Some committee members asked when London started the measured service billing system. Brown replied that when the British Post Office took over the telephone business, it specially allowed some users to continue using the metered rate system. However, by 1921, the authorities felt tired of that method and notified the old users, announcing that the metered rate system would be terminated, and the measured service billing system was universally implemented in that year. Moreover, what London implemented was a complete measured service billing system, with no first stage of free calls included. Brown further said that before the measured service billing system was uniformly implemented, the average number of calls in London and other places was 7.5 times per day. After the measured service billing system was implemented, the number of calls dropped to just over 5 times per day, a reduction of 25%. However, in Tokyo, Japan, the number of calls was reduced by 50% after the measured service billing system was implemented. The higher the original number of calls, the greater the degree of reduction in the future. If Shanghai is concerned, the degree of reduction will exceed that of London after the measured service billing system is implemented, but it may not be as large as in Tokyo, Japan. Although the metered rate system was used in England from 1879 to 1922, users were limited to a small number of old users who enjoyed special privileges. Furthermore, when the metered rate system was still in use in England, the average rental fee for commercial telephones was about £10 per year. After the post office took over, the monthly rental fee for commercial telephones in Liverpool was 12 shillings, and a fee of one penny was charged for each call. He had studied the situation in Shanghai and found it comparable. However, the fee of one penny per call in England is about twice as much as the proposed three cents in Shanghai.

The time for this expert investigation, research, and report was a total of two months. Some committee members asked if this time was sufficient. Brown said that this all depends on what kind of work they need to do. If all of the company's equipment needs to be evaluated one by one, the time required will be very long. When drafting this report, all of the financial reports and numbers were indeed provided by the telephone company, and the experts reviewed and determined them. On this point, it must be known that each expert has his own unique experience in equipment costs. Brown then gave a very detailed account of the method of calculating telephone set costs and the procedures for comparing costs in various places.

A committee member asked that since the prices of commercial and residential telephones have already been determined in the report, how much impact will the recent changes in exchange rates have on the telephone prices? Brown replied that they cannot change their recommendations due to fluctuations in exchange rates. He felt that internal costs would not increase significantly. A committee member also said that part of the company's costs is certainly related to exchange rates, such as the salaries of personnel calculated in gold dollars. Brown said that, as far as he knew, only one person's salary was calculated in gold dollars. The head of the SMC Finance Department also said that the experts' work cannot take into account exchange rate and other issues. Another committee member said that, according to the report, if the metered rate system is not changed, the company will have to increase its capital expenditure by about $3 million due to the continued increase in call volume. Fluctuations in exchange rates will certainly have a considerable impact on the company's expenditures. Brown said that he had not paid attention to or studied the exchange rate issue. The committee member immediately said that on this point, it can be seen that if the metered rate system continues, the future danger is indeed great.

Another committee member then discussed the valuation of the company's land, buildings, equipment, etc., and asked whether the experts had conducted in-depth investigations or only relied on the numbers in the company's accounts. Brown said that it would be unfair to say that the experts only relied on the company's accounts. Because the reason why an expert is an expert is that he must have considerable experience in these matters and must not only rely on the company's accounts as a basis, but must review each number. However, the valuation is a very complicated issue. Taking the example of the British Post Office, after the bureau took over the telephone business, it originally planned to conduct property valuations every five years, but later found the work too heavy. It took about 20 years from the time it took over the assets of the National Telephone Company to complete one valuation. At that time, there was a so-called percentage standard, which was the standard for all costs before the war. After the end of the European War, prices increased, reaching 120% by 1922. Moreover, the equipment at that time was old and urgently needed to be reformed, so the expenditure was even greater. Although the prices were very high, it could not be avoided. Afterwards, prices gradually declined until 1929, but during this period, the average price was still 80% or 90% above the pre-war price. As a result, equipment estimated at £30 million according to pre-war prices amounted to £100 million in total investment after the war. Moreover, the valuation must be carried out on a certain definite date, but under this situation, how to give it an appropriate valuation is indeed a question. If you want to do it with the Shanghai Telephone Company, you may need to hire at least 50 people and take a year. But after the valuation is agreed upon, if you do it a month later, the numbers obtained will definitely be different from the previous ones.

A committee member immediately stated that, according to Brown's statement, the experts did indeed have to rely on the company's accounts with a heavy heart. Brown expressed absolute disagreement with this. He said that the experts used their own experience to judge all the numbers provided by the company. Although the experts do not have expertise in the valuation of land and buildings, they still obtain independent valuations from time to time and have the SMC Works Department review them. If an explanation is needed, such as the high cost of the foundation of the Fujian Road branch, then a further investigation will be conducted. Therefore, anyone who knows of a better valuation method, he will sincerely welcome it.

Regarding company personnel and salaries, Hu Ruixiang stated that the total number of company personnel is 913, the average salary is $132.49 per month, and the total monthly salary is approximately $121,000. Detailed numbers can also be provided if needed. The head of the Finance Department immediately stated that the company's current salary grades do not affect the telephone prices proposed by the experts. Moreover, the company's salaries are not too high, and are roughly equal to those in other public utilities. The company has also recently implemented streamlining and saved a lot.

The committee members then discussed the issue of the length of calls. It is obviously unfair to charge the same fee for a one-minute call as for a ten-minute call. Furthermore, ineffective calls are also a problem. How should it be calculated when it often takes three or four calls to find the person you are looking for? Brown acknowledged that it is indeed unfair to charge the same fee regardless of the length of time. However, in order to achieve fairness, the company will have to add a three-cent metering device. Telephone authorities in various countries have long taken into account the possibility of this abuse. However, the second point has nothing to do with the company. Since the company provides users with a reasonable supply, the user should not be blamed on the company even if it takes three or four calls to find the person they are looking for. However, the time-based accounting method is often implemented when the call exceeds the range of the central station. This has also been done in London. Within the London line, the duration of the call is not limited at all. Although the company is taking some risks, there are only a few people who talk endlessly. If the scope of the call exceeds the London line, it must be calculated according to time. However, if this method is implemented in this city, the voices of opposition from all walks of life will inevitably erupt and become unstoppable. The public's attacks will probably be ten or a hundred times more intense than the current opposition to measured service billing. Therefore, the introduction of this problem has considerable danger.

Furthermore, the number of users who are willing to accept the measured service billing system has also been discussed. According to what has been expressed by the Chinese Chamber of Commerce, the majority of Chinese users are in favor of the metered rate system and have made preparations to pay by meter. Brown said that the current opposition to the measured service billing system comes from organized groups who feel that they will suffer losses. However, there is no opposition from those who pay the price for large users. The experts have made thousands of estimates on this point, and have made precise calculations on what kind of users make how many calls per month. A committee member then asked whether the experts had ignored the strong expression of support for the metered rate system from Chinese users. Brown said that what can be told now is that the experts' conclusion that the measured service billing system is feasible has nothing to do with this kind of argument. The experts' conclusion is based on scientific principles. He personally has not discovered any special characteristics of Shanghai users. If there is any, it is the method of using the telephone that is no longer seen elsewhere, but can still be seen here.

The head of the Finance Department then expressed his opinion, saying that what is needed now is to seek the greatest benefit for the majority. Since it has been proven that under the metered rate system, part of the telephone fees paid by small users is paid by large users, if the metered rate system is still used in disregard of the experts' advice, equipment and the like must continue to be added in the future, and the number of profits will inevitably increase accordingly. If there is no hope of reducing the company's demands, the increase in telephone prices in the future will be not only 11%, but 26%, and the decrease in telephone sets in the future has not yet been taken into account. In that case, users will unknowingly be subjected to even greater price increase demands. As capital investment increases day by day, telephone prices will inevitably rise accordingly. Therefore, price increase problems like today's will become more and more frequent. The company has no way to develop its own organization and obtain considerable profits. Therefore, according to what he has seen, if profits are to be obtained without harming the majority of users, that is, small users, there is really no good industry other than the measured service billing system. If the metered rate system continues to be used for a long time, the situation will get worse and worse in the future. By the end of 1936, the company's profit shortfall will reach $700,000. At that time, if the metered rate system is still used, the only way to recover that loss is to increase prices again. However, under the measured service billing system, the company has a hope of gradually obtaining profits. Once the profits reach that number or exceed it, the telephone price revision account can be applied at any time, and the telephone price can be reduced.

Regarding the number of calls, he really could not understand that the number of calls would not decrease after the measured service billing system was adopted. The head of the Finance Department added that the company has agreed to a one-year trial. In the future, if the profit exceeds one point, it will be included in the telephone fee revision for better or worse. Rae said that if the reduction in the number of calls in the future exceeds 37.5%, the company will inevitably ask the SMC to increase prices again. The head of the Finance Department admitted his statement, but according to what he has seen, this danger is smaller than the danger of continuing to use the metered rate system, because the number that should be added under the metered rate system is extremely large.

Brown compared the value of the telephone for users with other methods of communicating information, and found that the telephone fees under the measured service billing system are actually very low. However, if a user makes 6,000 or 7,000 calls per year, the telephone prices paid in the future will inevitably be higher than now.

A committee member then raised two points: one is the current situation in Shanghai. Although this situation has been mentioned in the latter part of the report, it has not been comprehensively calculated. The second point is that the experts did not have enough time to complete their investigation work. Therefore, the consideration of the economic situation of this city is the responsibility of the Public Utilities Committee. Although the public's voice is not long enough, it should also be taken into consideration. Furthermore, a 37.5% reduction in call volume, in his opinion, is still an ideal loss and has not yet been realized. The company should not increase the burden on the public in advance. Furthermore, under the current situation, the SMC's 2% annual tax should be temporarily suspended. The head of the Finance Department said that the SMC's annual tax does not have a deep relationship with the proposed telephone prices. Another committee member said that although he attaches great importance to the work of the experts, he supports their report because he feels that the experts did not have enough time during the investigation, so they had to use the numbers provided by the company as a basis for calculation, making the price increase an inevitable conclusion. Furthermore, the experts did not collect as much user opinions as possible, and the reasons why the metered rate system should be continued were not fully considered. He advocated that even though time is extremely short, experts should contribute their opinions again. He had to express his regret for not being able to support the report. The chairman declared again that no matter what proposals the committee members make on this issue, the company's consent is still needed, because the SMC cannot order the company, but must reach an agreement with it. The acting director-general of the SMC added that the company is demanding a price increase due to insufficient profits, and the SMC has to grant its request. However, if the prices proposed by the SMC still cannot give the company the profits it deserves, the company may refuse to accept them and submit the price increase issue to mediation. As for the measured service billing system, although the French Concession SMC has not yet expressed its opinion, there is a lot of support. If this Bureau's Public Utilities Committee does not support the experts' advocacy of measured service billing and the French SMC supports it, this Bureau's prestige will suffer a great loss. The head of the Finance Department said that regarding the SMC's annual tax, if the SMC is willing to give it up, the number of revenue shortages must still be shared among the citizens, and the majority of the citizens are still telephone users.

Then Brown, Rae, and others made a simple comparison of the first stage of call volume with the existing systems in other countries. Finally, the expert report was approved by the SMC Public Utilities Committee with a majority. The chairman finally thanked the experts for their work, and then adjourned the meeting.

Shanghai Textile Industry Overview 100

— Compiled by China Credit Information Office

(One of the Overviews of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

1. The Evolution and Status of Shanghai's Textile Industry

Spinning and weaving have a long history, but machine manufacturing has only about forty years of history in our country. It was only after the import of machine-made cotton fabrics from British India that the Chinese began to imitate them. In the sixteenth year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty (that is, twenty-two years before the founding of the Republic of China), Li Hongzhang established the Machine Weaving Factory (commonly known as the Foreign Cloth Bureau) in Yangshupu, Shanghai, which was the beginning of Shanghai's textile industry and also the beginning of the yarn industry in the whole country. After that, the development of Shanghai's yarn industry can be observed in three major stages.

First, the initial stage—from the Sino-Japanese War in the twenty-first year of Guangxu, through the Russo-Japanese War, (the twenty-first year of Guangxu) to the European War in the third year of the Republic of China, was the initial stage of Shanghai's textile industry. During this period, the main actors were foreign merchants, such as Ruiji of the German merchants (later changed to British merchants), Hongyuan of the American merchants (later from British to Japanese), Yih and of the British merchants, and Donghua and other factories of the Japanese merchants, all of which were established in Shanghai after the Sino-Japanese War. Later, although Chinese merchants established Zhenhua, Jiucheng, Tongchang, and other factories, most of them were small in scale or jointly operated with foreign capital, and they were not unique. Therefore, coupled with the various malpractices of official and private joint ventures at that time, the difficulties encountered by Shanghai's textile industry in the initial stage were numerous.

Second, the rising stage—the European War and the years after the war were the rising stage of Shanghai's textile industry, and also the golden age of our country's yarn industry. Because at that time, except for Japan in the east, European countries were busy with the war and post-war reconstruction work and had no time to look eastward. Indian cotton and Indian yarn, which dominated the country, temporarily retreated, and the national yarn industry took the opportunity to rise. According to statistics, about twenty or more Chinese yarn factories, such as Shenxin, rose in Shanghai at that time. Among them, the most were added in the ninth year of the Republic of China, with a total of ten. However, the only drawback is that the Japanese yarn factories in Shanghai also increased at the same speed, and all of them were newly established. Unlike the Chinese merchants, some of them were reorganized. Therefore, the spindles added by Japanese merchants were 40,000 to 50,000, exceeding those of Chinese merchants by about 10,000 to 20,000. As a result, the power of foreign yarn factories in Shanghai is still strong and considerable today. This is what we should pay attention to.

Third, the difficult stage—after the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, the textile power of Western Europe came to the East again. After the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, the national industry and commerce were affected by the National Revolution. Therefore, it is difficult to say how Shanghai's yarn industry will develop. During the period of the silver devaluation, Shanghai's yarn industry flourished for a while, but it was very short-lived. After the September 18th Incident, our country's politics was frequently affected by special influences. Last year, it was hit by the United States' silver purchase policy. Shanghai's textile industry (and the whole country as well) fell into extreme difficulties. Yarn sales were stagnant, inventories piled up, and factories stopped work or closed down. It has not yet recovered.

The evolution of Shanghai's textile industry has been briefly described above. Now, let's further discuss its position in the national textile industry. According to the investigation report of the Chinese Yarn Factory Association in March of this year, there are a total of 143 Chinese and foreign yarn factories in the country, and Shanghai accounts for 65, that is, 45.45% of the total number of factories in the country. In terms of Chinese factories alone, there are 95 in the country, and Shanghai accounts for 31, which also accounts for more than one-third. From this, it can be seen how important Shanghai's yarn industry is in the country.

2. Overview of Shanghai's Chinese Factories

From the previous section, we already know the importance of Shanghai's yarn industry. However, in recent years, due to the impact of various factors, it has also fallen into difficulties like the mainland. Now, let's list the major changes in Shanghai's Chinese factories in the past three years as follows:

Table of Changes in Shanghai Chinese Yarn Factories in the Past Three Years

In terms of the number of factories, there were three more in the twenty-second year of the Republic of China than in the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, and the twenty-third year of the Republic of China maintained the status quo. The future of the yarn industry seems to be stable. However, according to the actual situation, it is slightly different. Although the number of yarn spindles, thread spindles, and looms has increased, the actual number of workers or not increases in the same proportion. According to the Social Economic Monthly Report in Volume 2, Issue 7, of the 31 factories in the 22nd year, 9 factories reduced work and 8 factories stopped work. Among the total number of 1,126,204 yarn spindles, the number of spindles stopped and reduced reached more than one-fourth, totaling 365,124. Therefore, on the one hand, the number of factories, yarn spindles, etc. is increasing, while on the other hand, the number of workers and motive power is decreasing. After analysis, it seems that we cannot be optimistic.

Among the 31 existing factories in Shanghai, the earliest in history is the Hengfeng Textile New Bureau (its predecessor was the Foreign Cloth Bureau founded by Li Hongzhang), followed by Dongfang (that is, the current Shenxin No. 7 Factory), Tongchang Zhen, and the largest in capital are Shenxin Yongan, followed by Tongyi Dafeng, etc. The entire factories that have been shut down are Shenxin No. 2 and No. 5 Factories, and Tongchang Minsheng Jingwei Shanghai Textile Four Factories (to be continued).

The Path to Political System Reform (Continued) 109

— Pan Gongzhan (November 24th in Shanghai)

——Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang and the gentlemen who like to talk about political system reform——

If we say that if the political system is not reformed, the party rule will not be abolished, the tutelage will not end, and thus talents cannot be concentrated and civil rights cannot be developed; if talents are not concentrated and civil rights are not developed, then the heavy national crisis cannot be resolved. At first glance, it seems not unreasonable. However, if we investigate it slightly from the actual situation and political theory, then this seemingly right but actually wrong argument against the procedure set by the Founding Program can be broken without attack.

Why is that? First, I would like to ask, is "talent concentration" to be concentrated in "organization" or in "scattered"? Even a three-foot child knows that there must first be a considerable organization, and its organization must be strict, and then talent can be concentrated. Therefore, from "non-party" politics to "multi-party" politics (that is, the politics of party competition), and then from "multi-party" politics to "one-party" politics, is an inevitable trend of political evolution, and it is also an inevitable step from no organization to a strict organization. Now, on the one hand, we want to concentrate talents, but on the other hand, we want to retreat from "one-party" to "multi-party", and even from "multi-party" to "non-party", returning my Chinese compatriots to the original state of a plate of loose sand. Regardless of whether it greatly violates Sun Yat-sen's last wishes, even if it is done once, wouldn't it run counter to the original intention of concentrating talents? Therefore, today, if we don't talk about "concentrating talents", if we want to concentrate them, we can only recruit general real talents who believe in the Three People's Principles into the Kuomintang, or retreat ten steps or a hundred steps, and recruit real talents who can abide by the Three People's Principles under the Kuomintang government led by the Kuomintang, and work together to achieve the reality of concentration. Generally speaking, the more difficult the country is, the more urgent the need for political power to be concentrated, and the more natural the trend of talent to be concentrated. The Soviet Russia after the war, Italy after the march on Rome, and Germany after the success of the National Socialist Party need not be said. Even in the countries of Britain, France, Japan, and the United States, which have always had multi-party competition, there have been actions to merge into one, such as the British all-party cabinet, the French mixed cabinet, the Japanese extraordinary cabinet (and the cabinet deliberation council to recruit distinguished people), and the US Congress authorizing the president, all of which want to seek strategies to concentrate talents and concentrate power under the constitutional government of multi-party competition. It can be seen that all countries in the East and the West, because of the extraordinary times, hope to combine from division, and unlike our "celebrated scholars", they hope that my country's political system will retreat to the whirlpool of "multi-party" disturbance or "non-party" chaos before the 13th year of the Republic of China because of the dangerous national situation. Therefore, "concentrating talents" is one thing, and "abolishing party rule" is another. It must be known that "guest ministers" can still be used, let alone "compatriots"? If the party in power is loyal to the country, it will definitely be happy to use the talents of the world, as long as these talents are not vowed to betray the party that built the country. Although the Soviet Russia is a socialist country under the dictatorship of the Communist Party, why haven't talents been concentrated in the two five-year plans? Although Italy and Germany are countries under the dictatorship of the Fascist Party or the National Socialist Party, why haven't talents been concentrated in the process of building the country at home and abroad? Those who are unwilling to gather are only those who are incompatible with the doctrine of building the country, and how can those who govern the country please everyone? Take the current China as an example, there are indeed many facts that non-party talents are accommodated. There is also the possibility of concentration. Not only are the heads of local governments and administrative regions rare among non-party talents, but even in the central government, various departments and committees, many scholars, are not entirely affiliated with the party. From this, it can be seen that even if the party rule is not abolished, talents can also be concentrated, and there is no inevitable causal relationship between the two.

Second, I would like to ask whether the exercise of civil rights requires training? If training is required, then the element of tutelage lies in training the exercise of civil rights and serving as a stepping stone for the implementation of constitutional government. Therefore, the more complete the tutelage today, the more proper the exercise of civil rights will be in the future, and the better the results of the constitutional government will be. As long as you have read the Founding Program personally written by Sun Yat-sen, you can understand this truth. If it is said that civil rights cannot be developed if the tutelage is not ended, then why should there be a stage of tutelage after the initial military stability and national unification? National education is not universal. The common sense of participation in politics is not available. The exercise of the four powers is not skilled. Local autonomy is not complete. With this to talk about civil rights and constitutional government, the result of it is that the civil government will be built on the beach. The lessons of the past are not far away. Just flipping through the history of the twelve or three years after the founding of the Republic of China will make you suddenly realize! The reason why Sun Yat-sen personally wrote the Founding Program in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China was to learn from the past and thoroughly build a very solid foundation for the civil government. Now, suppose we are again moved by the illusory rhetoric of those self-righteous "celebrated scholars" and shake our beliefs, regardless of the degree of popular wisdom, regardless of the effectiveness of the tutelage, and think that the tutelage may as well end and the constitution can be implemented immediately, then not only will the previous achievements be abandoned, but the constitution that is hastily implemented will also end up showing a phenomenon that is neither a donkey nor a horse. Hu Shi believes that "constitutional government is the best training for constitutional government" is actually a kind of evasion. It must be known that the period of training constitutional government, in the Kuomintang, is called tutelage, which is also the tutelage mentioned in the Founding Program. The provisional constitution during the tutelage period is also the constitution during the training of constitutional government. Therefore, the need for training in constitutional government has been recognized by those who oppose tutelage and does not need to be more verbose. What needs to be explained is that the constitution is the fundamental law of the country, and the promulgation of the constitution was originally a matter that should be taken very seriously. However, to think that the tutelage has been completed once the constitution is promulgated, and the constitution must be promulgated once the constitutional government has begun, is a big mistake! Article 22 of the Founding Program states: "The draft constitution shall be based on the Founding Program and the achievements of the two periods of tutelage and constitutional government, and shall be discussed and decided by the Legislative Yuan. It shall be publicized to the people at any time in preparation for adoption and implementation at the appropriate time." Since the draft constitution is said to be based on the achievements of the two periods of tutelage and constitutional government, it can be seen that the period of constitutional government is before the discussion and decision of the draft constitution. The so-called "period of constitutional government" here probably refers to Article 16 and Article 19 "the period when constitutional government begins". Now there is not a province that can see that all the counties have reached complete self-government. Originally, even "the period when constitutional government begins" cannot be talked about. For the time being, retreat ten steps or a hundred steps, then the current China, even if it wants to leapfrog and advance, will at most step into the stage of "the period when constitutional government begins". Therefore, if it is not for the sake of decorating the facade, then the provisional constitution during the tutelage period is really the fundamental law of "the period when constitutional government begins". With this provisional constitution, it can be used well, obeyed well, can train civil rights as much as possible, and can develop civil rights as much as possible. If we must formulate another constitution, we only need to discuss and decide on a draft constitution that can be applied in the early stage of constitutional government, which must contain the spirit of tutelage to the appropriate extent so that civil rights can be intensified in training within the appropriate scope, and only then can it truly be beneficial to the country and benefit the people. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 110

— (Allegory)

According to the September issue of the English Modern Historical Materials Magazine, it is said that there are many Westerners who can speak Chinese, but only twelve who can write Chinese.

Reading Thomas De Quincy's "Confessions of an Opium Eater", I learned that he once knew a street prostitute who was very kind to him. Are these street prostitutes also like the prostitutes on the Fourth Malu in Shanghai?

In Vienna, if you want to avoid being suspected of being a member of the National Socialist Party, you only need to drink beer with relish, because members of the National Socialist Party in Austria resist it because the beer tax is high.

A 75-year-old white-haired candle maker in New York claims that someone recently asked him to customize a huge candle to commemorate the former band leader and film actor named Ross Columbus, which must burn for a thousand years. This candle maker's name is Enduni Ajelo, and he is known for making the world's finest candles. He refused to disclose the name of the person who customized this giant candle, only saying that it was an unmarried woman from somewhere in California.

Wushan Crispy Cake 111

— Shu Fan

The crispy cake in Wushan Four Scenery Garden is fatty, tender, sweet and loose, and was praised by diners in the Qing Dynasty, no less than the Song Sao fish soup by the West Lake. Whenever there was a provincial examination, the Zhejiang candidates would all try it once for pleasure. At that time, the incense of the City God Mountain was in full bloom, and the guests had to stay there, drinking tea and eating. Therefore, the business was booming, and it was vaguely opposed to the Five Willows Residence. Since the Republic of China, the shops in the upper city have gradually moved north, and Yunjuliang Road! All the mountain names belong to Wushan! The area has become a trace of the past. Now, if you ask about the Four Scenery Garden, even the people of Hangzhou will be stunned and unable to answer. The garden is located on the sunny side of the mountain, with low buildings and empty ridges, which are extremely high, refreshing, broad and clean; the trees are hidden on the left and right, and the wind can make the sound of autumn waves; facing the Qiantang River, looking at the desolate white practice, swallowing and spitting the shadows of sails, it makes people feel the sense of washing away the remaining heroes! And the fireworks of Xixing across the bank, coming out of the forest silk by silk, are no less than a picture of a maid washing her hair. It is a pity that such a good view is rarely seen by the guests. According to Yun Jiao: In the past, when Zhang Nan first came to Zhejiang, he had to come here with a staff and a book every day to drink tea, which can be said to be the confidant of the garden. Later, he called for cakes to be made, which was managed by an old woman. When asked, it has been dozens of years; and she told the story of the rise and fall. Thinking of a cake like this, why listen to the white-haired palace maid? The woman's face showed a vegetable color, and we could not bear to ask again. The cake is boiled in oil. When it is cooked, it can be separated by touching the finger, so it is incomparably crispy. When leaving, the sun was setting, looking at the fourth floor was still empty, and no one continued to us, it was a great sorrow! Then wrote a poem: "The Wushan woman is like a paragraph, try to see the short-haired frost in the living; at noon, the high-rise is empty, and the diners pity a cake with vicissitudes!" But what can it make up for?

Two Typical Characters 112

— Zhu Ying

Living in a house at the end of the alley are Mr. He and Mr. Yuan.

These two gentlemen can truly represent typical characters in two environments.

Mr. He is a person who loves gambling like his life. Unless he has no money in his hand. There is nothing to say. If he has money in his hand, he will gamble day and night, forgetting to eat and sleep. If he gambles smoothly, then it seems that he has made a fortune. He buys fish and meat, and sometimes pulls some relatives and friends to his house to eat and drink. He takes his wife to watch movies, go to the Great World, eat big meals, and ride in cars. If the child wants money, he always gives two hairs at a time. But if he loses the gamble, then he will not open his mouth all day. If the child makes a noise, he will raise his leg and kick his butt. If his wife says to him that the rice jar is empty, or that the rent should be paid tomorrow, then he will clench his fist and hit the table so hard that the things on the table will jump straight up, and he will have to yell with a loud voice: "You only know how to eat and die, I am not a robber, earning money is so easy!"

Mr. Yuan, however, is not like this. All day long, he just faces a lamp as big as a mung bean and smokes opium. If his wife asks him for a dollar to buy rice, he just pretends not to hear it. He will absolutely refuse to open his wallet until she opens her mouth for the third time. But when the opium ash container has not seen the bottom, he has already prepared to fry it. All year round, if he has money, he will fry and smoke more opium, and his face will be smiling. If he has no money, he will fry and smoke less, and the smile on his face will be reduced. He does not ask about family affairs at all, except for the separate account that his wife makes for buying food every day. Sometimes he may say a word or two, "Why do you spend so much, a dollar has been spent in three days", but he has never been harsh.

One day, Mrs. He said to Mrs. Yuan, "Your Mr. Yuan is still good. He is patient."

Mrs. Yuan replied with a mournful face, "Enough, asking him for a dollar is like asking for his life."

Butterfly Loves Flowers (Immortal Figure of Mount Luofu) 114

Her reputation as a beauty is as high as the Big Dipper.

There's no way to make the peach blossoms wither.

It's written into the verses of the Book of Odes.

Little Western Paradise 116

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-One: She Softly Relies on Him, Cherishing Her Moon-like Beauty; He Vigorously Admonishes His Son-in-Law, Listening to the Lion's Roar from the Next Room

Although Jia Duocai didn't say anything, his face was very unsightly. He looked at the opposite room and saw several women's shadows in the window. He stretched out two diagonal lines on either side of his nose and gave Zhou Tai a bitter smile. Zhou Tai said, "I know Mr. Jia must be unhappy, but this has nothing to do with your wife. If you want to blame someone, blame me." As Zhou Tai spoke, she originally wanted to cover up for Yueying, but Yueying had already glanced over from the window, seeing Jia Duocai's small mustache turned up, his two lychee eyes staring, and his face red. Her heart was pounding wildly, and she figured that even with Zhou Tai as her bodyguard, this matter wouldn't ease up, so it would be better to go out early and admit her mistake to end the scene. So, with her right hand twisting the buttons on her collar and her left hand behind her back, she bit her lip and went out of the room, slanting her body. When she reached the hallway, she stopped again, hiding behind Zhou Tai. Because her footsteps were so light, Zhou Tai didn't hear her until she was right next to her. At this time, Jia Duocai's eyes were only looking at Zhou Tai's back, so she also turned her head and saw Yueying standing with her head lowered. She looked at both sides, then grasped Yueying's drooping hand and said, "Even if you want to be a virtuous wife and loving mother, you don't have to be so scared of your husband, like a mouse seeing a cat." As she spoke, she pulled her forward. At this moment, Wang Beihai, carrying a book bag, rushed in in a hurry. He was rushing so forcefully that he didn't notice there were acquaintances beside him. Only when he reached the front did they dodge each other and stop. (360)

Fragrant Shadows of the Imperial Incense 117

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

She was also impatient to sit in the hall any longer, so she hurriedly announced the end of the court session, and we still escorted her back to the palace. Usually, when the Empress Dowager returned to the palace, she would always look around and inspect everywhere along the way. Today, however, she walked straight ahead without taking her eyes off the road, directly back to her bedroom. The flowers blooming in various parts of the garden were always loved by the old woman, but today, although there were also several kinds of bright seasonal flowers blooming, they no longer aroused any good feelings in her; even the little eunuchs in various places kowtowing to her as usual when she passed by could no longer win a glance from her.

Usually, her body was a little hunched, but today she stood very straight, like a very brave young monarch; she seemed to want to stand her own body on the body of her enemy and press him down hard, so that he would not have the opportunity to climb up and defeat her. Now she felt the weight of the responsibility on her shoulders!

I couldn't help but suspect secretly: Perhaps this sudden change was the result of the very flustered and urgent omen that everyone felt when we returned from Fengtian!

After the Empress Dowager returned to her bedroom, she impatiently ordered everyone to leave together, only allowing two female officials to stay and serve her, and I was one of those two. That poor Guangxu, although in name was still a "current" emperor, was never allowed to be involved in any major national affairs (even minor matters did not give him a chance to express his opinion). Naturally, he had already been sent away by the Empress Dowager. Even Empress Longyu and Consort Jin were ordered to leave at the same time; the other palace maids and eunuchs were even more decisively driven out by the Empress Dowager. (456)

Short Story

Personality 118

— Zhu Xun

Mr. Wu was the chief editor of a small newspaper in the interior, and it had been two years since he started. In this kind of year, national affairs were certainly not the concern of small newspapers, but for the sake of public opinion, local affairs could not but be handled impartially, with an honest pen. Mr. Wu was originally a fool confined in his study. At first, he wanted to use this worn-out pen as three thousand Mauser rifles, to bring light to dark places, and to fight a bright path in the dark society!

Mr. Wu's foolish plan was put into practice for a few months, alas! The darkness of society became even thicker; and Mr. Wu's mental and physical pain was enough for him to endure. Summons from the court flew in one after another, and court hearings and trials became commonplace. However, the people in society, apart from a few close friends, still maintained considerable friendship with Mr. Wu; the rest of the people had heard of Mr. Wu's great name and shook their heads at him, especially a group of gentry gentlemen, who regarded him as a thoroughly troublemaking bad guy!

In addition to dealing with the law, Mr. Wu also suffered several major insults and injuries. After being insulted, he often scratched his graying head and said resentfully, "Editing a small newspaper is really not something a human does!" However, in this time of overstaffing, what else could he do? Moreover, because Mr. Wu had repeatedly been insulted, the newspaper owner had increased his salary from seventeen yuan to twenty-four silver dollars. He was grateful to his confidant, so of course he had to continue.

"I have my own noble personality, and right and wrong have their own public opinion, what am I afraid of!" After being stimulated, he often used this kind of Ah Q-like tone to comfort himself!

However, in this kind of environment, Mr. Wu's courage to fight naturally could not be mustered; his weak body could not withstand other people's fists, and because the small newspaper in the interior had no reporters and the manuscript fees were so small that they were equivalent to nothing, most of the articles in the newspaper were written by the editor. Mr. Wu changed his style and talked about trivial matters, so the sharp spirit of the newspaper gradually disappeared and gradually became a "gentleman's newspaper."

However, unfortunately, Mr. Wu got into a dispute again because of a manuscript: The manuscript was sent by a reporter from a major newspaper. The content of the article was a news report about the death of a certain bureau chief's wife. In an environment where it was not daring to scold people, this kind of seemingly mediocre but not common news was of course good material for a small newspaper, and the author was also a reporter running errands for that agency, so of course there would be no rumors; however, after it was published, a friend suddenly ran to Mr. Wu and said, "Old Wu: What mess have you made again? The unmarried wife of a certain sub-bureau chief is alive and well, how did you create such a rumor? Now a certain bureau chief, because of the news in the newspaper, has received more than a dozen mourning telegrams, is furious, and has hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit, and it must be resolved legally." Mr. Wu, hearing that the news was inaccurate, of course felt apologetic in his heart, so he wanted to ask that friend to mediate, but that friend shook his head and said, "I have already spoken to him for you, but he refused outright and really can't help."

In this kind of environment, Mr. Wu could not but make legal defense work. The first step was to bring the reporter who wrote the manuscript to ask about the source of the news. That reporter busily took out a mourning strip reporting the death of a certain bureau chief's wife, and it was printed with a certain bureau's mailing address, so of course it was not a rumor made by a friend. So, in order to make an investigation, Mr. Wu also collected several newspaper strips from other newspaper offices. Fortunately, a certain boss in the newspaper office was newly appointed as a lawyer, so Mr. Wu went to visit him to inquire about legal protection. That boss was particularly happy that day and told Mr. Wu that there was no problem at all. Unless a certain bureau chief sent a letter to correct the error, let him file a lawsuit and ignore it.

After Mr. Wu got the guarantee from a certain boss, he returned to the office very confidently, but that friend who reported the news was already waiting in the editorial office, and opened his mouth to say, "A certain bureau chief has voluntarily reconciled, as long as you publish a correction notice, the matter will pass." Mr. Wu of course refused outright at first, but he couldn't stand that friend's repeated requests. Mr. Wu thought of that friend's intention, which was always well-intentioned, and lawsuits were not a happy thing after all, so Mr. Wu disobeyed a certain boss's orders and wrote another piece of corrected news; as a result, the situation became big, a certain boss was furious, and Mr. Wu's rice bowl was declared broken because of the boss's anger.

Mr. Wu stepped out of the newspaper office and stood blankly on the street corner: He thought of his future life, he thought of the boss's power, he thought of his friend's friendship. The setting sun gradually went down, and Mr. Wu's shadow became longer and longer; he was at a loss, vaguely saying: "I have my own noble personality, what am I afraid of!…"

Educational News

Ministry of Education Orders: Measures for Dividing Elementary School Districts in Cities and Counties 119

Measures for Investigating School-Age Children

The Ministry of Education issued an order on the 11th to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating that the division of elementary school districts and the investigation of school-age children are basic tasks for implementing compulsory education. In order to facilitate the handling of these tasks in various places, the Ministry has already formulated and promulgated the Measures for Dividing Elementary School Districts in Cities and Counties and the Measures for Investigating School-Age Children. The relevant measures are hereby issued for your compliance. This order.

Measures for Dividing Elementary School Districts in Cities and Counties

1. Each city and county shall follow the provisions of Article 9 of the Interim Measures Outline for Implementing Compulsory Education to divide the entire city and county into several elementary school districts as the smallest unit for implementing compulsory education.

2. The division of elementary school districts should be based on the density of the population, the interrelationship between the terrain and transportation, and with reference to the situation of local self-governing organizations.

3. The scope of an elementary school district should be based on a population of approximately one thousand people per district, but this may be varied in densely populated areas in cities.

4. Remote rural areas that are too far apart from other rural areas and have a population of less than one thousand may also be divided into one elementary school district.

5. Each elementary school district shall have one school supervisor, who shall be selected and appointed by the competent educational administrative agency from local people with prestige. Assistant personnel may also be appointed as appropriate, depending on the complexity of the affairs, to assist.

6. For the convenience of management, each city and county should establish a joint elementary school district by combining five to ten elementary school districts from the original autonomous regions.

7. Each joint elementary school district shall have one education commissioner, who shall be selected by the competent educational administrative agency from the outstanding elementary school principals in the district to serve concurrently.

8. Elementary school districts in remote rural areas may adopt mobile teaching or other methods to teach out-of-school children.

9. When each county and city completes the division of elementary school districts, it shall report the handling situation in detail to the provincial education department for review.

10. When each province and city completes the division of elementary school districts in the entire province and city, it shall report the handling situation in detail to the Ministry of Education for review.

11. These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Measures for Investigating School-Age Children

1. The competent educational administrative agencies of each province, county, city, and directly administered municipality under the Executive Yuan shall clearly investigate the number of school-age children in the year before the start of each academic year.

2. The investigation of school-age children shall be carried out by elementary school district, and the number of children already enrolled in each elementary school district and the number of out-of-school children shall be investigated together.

3. The investigation of school-age children shall be the responsibility of the school supervisors of each elementary school district, and the county and city competent educational administrative agencies shall supervise and urge them to carry out the investigation. The elementary school teachers and staff of each elementary school district that has already established a primary school shall assist the school supervisors in handling the investigation.

4. County magistrates, public security bureau chiefs, district chiefs, steel chiefs, township chiefs, bao chiefs, jia chiefs, etc. shall all assist in handling the investigation of school-age children.

5. When necessary, the investigation of school-age children may be carried out by the public security bureau sending police to notify households to facilitate the investigation.

6. When each elementary school district completes the investigation of school-age children, it shall immediately create true forms and reports to the education commissioner. The education commissioner shall clearly count the results of the investigation in each elementary school district and create a form and report to the competent educational administrative agency. The competent educational administrative agency may send personnel to each elementary school district for spot checks. If any false investigations are encountered, a re-investigation should be strictly ordered.

7. When each county and city completes the investigation of school-age children in the entire county and city, it shall immediately count them clearly, create a form, and report to the provincial education department for review. The provincial education department may send personnel to various counties for spot checks. If any false investigations are encountered, a re-investigation should be strictly ordered.

8. When each province and city completes the investigation of school-age children in the entire province and city, it shall immediately count them clearly, create a form, and report to the Ministry of Education for filing at the beginning of each academic year.

9. The various forms used for the investigation of school-age children shall be determined separately by the Ministry of Education.

10. The funds required for the investigation of school-age children in each province, city, county, and city shall be raised by themselves and submitted to the higher-level agency for filing.

11. The investigation of school-age children in each locality shall be fully publicized in advance so that the public can generally understand it to avoid resistance.

12. If anyone is found to be instigating obstruction during the investigation of school-age children, the local competent authority shall strictly punish them in accordance with the law.

13. These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Record of Chairman Lin's Inspection of Education in Fujian 120

Inspected a total of eleven schools and social education institutions, and believes that education in Fujian Province has made great progress compared to the past

When Chairman Lin of the National Government returned to Fujian to pay his respects to his ancestors, he not only inquired in detail about the handling of education in Fujian Province from Education Director Zheng and praised it deeply, but also returned to his hometown on October 17 to participate in the completion ceremony of the new school building of Fenghang Elementary School, and personally delivered a speech to encourage the children of his hometown to work hard and make progress. The elementary school was built by Chairman Lin at his own expense two years ago, and it is well-managed. On the morning of the 21st, he went to the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou Normal School for inspection with Military Advisor Mao and Education Director Zheng. After inspecting the newly built auditorium and classrooms for a week, he went to the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou No. 3 Elementary School to visit Sun Yat-Sen Hall. This hall was originally the Qing Dynasty's Minglun Hall. When President Sun came to Fujian in the first year of the Republic of China, he lectured there. In order to commemorate the President, people from all walks of life renamed it Sun Yat-Sen Hall. It is currently being renovated with funds allocated by the Central Party Department at the joint request of Chen Xiongbao and Chairman Chen Gongru. At nine o'clock, he went to the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou High School. The principal and teachers of the school respectfully welcomed him at the door. More than 800 male and female students, all wearing uniforms, gathered in the large playground and lined up to pay their respects. The Chairman expressed his extreme satisfaction with the neatness and cleanliness of the school and the students' lively spirit. At ten o'clock, when he went to visit the Provincial Science Museum, high school students in the museum's physics, biology, and chemistry departments were all practicing. The Chairman greatly praised the students' spirit and interest in studying science, and especially praised the museum's thorough and economical equipment and orderly management. He also lingered for a long time on the equipment of the weather station and the arrangement of the animal enclosure, and took photos at the museum as a souvenir. At eleven o'clock, he went to the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou No. 1 Elementary School. This school is a famous elementary school in Fuzhou. About 1,800 students lined up in the large playground to perform health exercises. Their clothes were clean and their steps were orderly, which greatly pleased the old man. Afterwards, he went to the Provincial Short-Term Compulsory Simple Elementary School. The school used an old General Temple as a school building. Most of the students were poor children, about 200 people. Chairman Lin believed that the two-part system and complex teaching method practiced by the school were particularly suitable. After the inspection of the prefecture was completed, he went to the Provincial Library to visit. In the afternoon, he went to the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou No. 2 Elementary School. The school's products won the Ministry of Education's greatest praise at last year's National Elementary and Middle School Labor Achievement Exhibition. At that time, when the Chairman visited the venue in Beijing, he also gave it a high rating. On this day, in addition to the personal inspection, he also the principal of the school and the labor science teacher guided the students in making various items such as human-faced bamboo earth batteries and flower baskets, etc., and sent them to on the 26th of the month to be exhibited in Beijing. He also personally wrote the four characters "Happy Education Cultivating Talents" and gave them to the school. Afterwards, he went to the Commercial Press to purchase various practical books about children and bestowed them on the school. At nine o'clock on the morning of the 23rd, he visited the Fujian College, inspected the classrooms, dormitories, farm, experimental rooms, family study rooms, etc., and finally went to the private Guangfu High School, where he spoke to the students for about 30 minutes, and toured the weaving department and the industrial field. In total, Chairman Lin inspected four ordinary elementary schools, one short-term elementary school, two middle schools, one normal school, one college, and two new education institutions. He believes that education in Fujian Province has made much progress compared to the last time he returned to Fujian, and has given many encouragement to the educational authorities.

In particular, German Ambassador Trautmann lingered in the venue, praising Wang's art, which can be included in the highest position in the world art scene. His works have been reserved and purchased by guests, such as the ink paintings No. 1 "Flood Map," No. 32 "Outside Gusu City," No. 21 "Lu Fangweng's Reading Place," No. 33 "Hong Kong Night Rain," and the extra edition of two paintings of "Laoshan Scenery." The oil paintings such as No. 47 "Jungle Liuxia," No. 51 "Test Ride," No. 57 "Laoshan Morning," No. 68 "Zhengyangmen Xiaose," No. 69 "White Pagoda Sunset," and No. 71 "West Lake Xiaose" all show the preciousness of Wang's works. Therefore, the Nanjing Capital Hotel has become lively, which is a good phenomenon of the capital's emerging art.

Shanghai Branch of the Educational Film Association Implements New Measures for Rotating Educational Films 124

The schools for the next week's rotation have been announced in advance. Schools that wish to change should notify in advance

Since the Shanghai Branch of the China Educational Film Association began to bury educational films in various schools on a weekly rotation, it has achieved remarkable results. Originally, it was planned to screen three times per school per semester, and four times per screening, which was not economical in terms of time. Therefore, it has been approved by the Education Bureau to revise the method, screening twice per school per semester, and increasing the number of films screened each time to six volumes. Each time, the schools and times for the next week's screenings will be announced first. If any schools wish to change, they can fill out a notification form and notify the association in advance. It is known that the association has announced the schools that will be screened next week, which are recorded as follows: Zuguang Elementary School at 3:00 PM on the 18th of this month, Shuji Elementary School at 6:00 PM, Peiben Elementary School at 8:30 PM, Cangji Elementary School at 2:00 PM on the 19th, Qingxin Girls' Middle School at 4:30 PM, Songxue Elementary School at 7:00 PM, Feihong Elementary School at 1:00 PM on the 20th, YMCA Middle School at 5:00 PM, Youde Elementary School at 7:30 PM, Qilu Elementary School at 10:00 AM on the 21st, Shangwen Elementary School at 2:30 PM, Xin Elementary School at 6:30 PM, Guangming Elementary School at 10:00 AM on the 22nd, Zhenru Elementary School at 7:00 PM, Xicheng Elementary School at 1:00 PM on the 23rd, Meixi Elementary School at 4:30 PM, and Nongtan Elementary School at 8:30 PM. Before each screening, the seats, curtain, and light-blocking black curtains should be prepared. If you want to make changes, please notify in advance.

China Education and Culture Foundation Continues to Provide Grants for Scientific Research 125

Those who request a grant must submit an application. The deadline is February 28 next year.

The Board of Directors of the China Education and Culture Foundation issued a notice yesterday, stating that the foundation has established a scientific research grant to promote scientific research, which has been handled in previous years. The scientific research grants are divided into three categories: A, B, and special. The research problems are limited to astronomy, meteorology, and earth science, arithmetic, physics, chemistry, biology, and their applications. Anyone who has received a grant from the foundation and wants to continue to request it, or who meets the qualifications of the three types of researchers set by the foundation and wants to request a grant from the foundation, can submit an application in accordance with the regulations for review. The deadline for the foundation to accept grant applications this year is February 28, 25. Applications submitted after the deadline will be included in the next round. Regarding the above detailed regulations and blank grant application forms, please send a letter to request them. Applicants who are abroad can request them from the embassy or the student supervision office in their country or neighboring country. Also, starting from this session, those who are recommended by the review committee as candidates for the research grant should go to the hospital or doctor designated by the foundation within one month after receiving the notice from the foundation for a physical examination (candidates residing abroad can go to the hospital or doctor designated by our country's embassy, consulate, or student supervision office on behalf of the foundation), obtain a health certificate, and send it to the foundation for verification. After the foundation has verified that there is no error, they can be elected. The foundation will pay for the above physical examination. If the candidate does not follow the above method to check the body and send the certificate to the foundation, or if the body is certified to be unhealthy after the examination, they will not be able to receive the research grant. This physical examination method must be followed uniformly regardless of whether it is a continued application or a new application. This is hereby announced.
