Current Situation of Henan University (Part 1)

The current situation of Henan Provincial Henan University is as follows:

I. General Outline of Organization

A. Administrative Section

The university has one president, who manages all university affairs. It has a Dean's Office, a Secretary's Office, a Library, and a Military Training Department, each responsible for their respective duties of academic affairs, administrative affairs, library matters, and military training. (1) Dean's Office: It has one dean, who consults with the president and assists in managing university affairs, and also oversees the three sections of Registration, Student Affairs, and Training. Each section has a director, section members, clerks, and secretaries. (2) Secretary's Office: It has one chief secretary and one secretary, who consult with the president and assist in managing university affairs, and also oversee the three sections of Documents, Accounting, and General Affairs. Each section has a director, section members, clerks, and secretaries. (3) Library: It has one library director, who, together with the dean, chief secretary, and deans of each college, consults with the president to handle all library affairs of the university. The library has clerks and secretaries. (4) Military Training Department: It has one military training director, four instructors, and two assistant instructors, who consult with the president and dean to handle all military training affairs of the university.

B. College Section

The university has five colleges. Except for the College of Medicine, which is not divided into departments for the time being, the four colleges of Liberal Arts, Science, Law, and Agriculture are divided into 12 departments in total. (1) College of Liberal Arts: three departments - Department of Chinese Literature and History, Department of English Literature, Department of Education. (2) College of Science: three departments - Department of Mathematics and Physics, Department of Chemistry, Department of Biology. (3) College of Law: three departments - Department of Law, Department of Political Science, Department of Economics. (4) College of Agriculture: three departments - Department of Agronomy, Department of Forestry, Department of Animal Husbandry. (5) College of Medicine: not divided into departments for the time being.

C. Affiliated Sections of Each College

The university, according to the nature of the colleges it has established, has the following affiliated sections: (1) Extension Education Department, jointly managed by each college. (2) Agricultural Farm, managed by the College of Agriculture. (3) Hospital, managed by the College of Medicine.

D. Affiliated Institutions

(1) Midwifery School and Obstetrics and Gynecology Hospital. (2) Henan Gazetteer Hall.

II. General Outline of the Curriculum

The university, this semester, has a total of 246 subjects, distributed among the colleges and departments as follows: (1) College of Liberal Arts: a total of 64 subjects - Department of Chinese Literature and History: 29 subjects; Department of English Literature: 15 subjects; Department of Education: 17 subjects; and affiliated Department of Sociology: 3 subjects. (Note) The Department of Sociology stopped enrolling students in the 22nd year. The students who enrolled in the 21st year are still in school. The department will be completely eliminated after they graduate in the 25th year. (2) College of Science: a total of 46 subjects - Department of Mathematics and Physics: 19 subjects; Department of Chemistry: 15 subjects; Department of Biology: 12 subjects. (3) College of Law: a total of 38 subjects - Department of Law: 13 subjects; Department of Political Science: 3 subjects; Department of Economics: 22 subjects. (Note) The Departments of Law and Political Science have stopped enrolling students. According to the Ministry's order, they should be abolished after the existing students graduate, and the Department of Economics should be merged into the College of Liberal Arts. (4) College of Agriculture: a total of 34 subjects - Department of Agronomy: 16 subjects; Department of Forestry: 10 subjects; Department of Animal Husbandry: 8 subjects. (5) College of Medicine: a total of 30 subjects. (6) Common required courses for each college: a total of 23 subjects. (7) Common elective courses for each college: a total of 11 subjects.

III. Number of Faculty Members

The university has a total of 70 professors, 17 lecturers, 11 general instructors, and 24 assistant instructors, distributed among the colleges as follows: (1) College of Liberal Arts: 22 professors, 3 lecturers, and 3 assistant instructors. (2) College of Science: 14 professors, 5 lecturers, and 9 assistant instructors. (3) College of Law: 9 professors, 5 lecturers, and 1 assistant instructor. (4) College of Agriculture: 9 professors, 1 lecturer, and 6 assistant instructors. (5) College of Medicine: 12 professors, 2 lecturers, and 3 assistant instructors. (6) Common required and elective courses for each college: 4 professors and 1 lecturer. (7) Physical education and military training courses: 11 instructors and 2 assistant instructors.

IV. Number of Staff Members

The university has a total of 65 staff members, distributed as follows: (1) President's Office: 2 people. (2) Dean's Office: 17 people (including 2 professors serving concurrently and 1 instructor serving concurrently). (3) Secretary's Office: 20 people (including 1 professor serving concurrently). (5) Military Training Department: 1 person. (6) Affiliated Hospital: 12 people (including 1 professor serving concurrently). (7) Affiliated Agricultural Farm: 5 people (including 1 assistant instructor serving concurrently). (To be continued)

Guangxia Middle School

Mr. Zhang Yuanruo, a legal expert and secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Government, was invited to Guangxia Middle School yesterday (the 11th) to attend the school's memorial week. More than 300 teachers and students attended. After the ceremony, Mr. Yan Xiyu Kai delivered an introductory speech, followed by a speech by Mr. Zhang, entitled "Self-Reliance and Youth Responsibility." He first explained the definition of self-reliance and explained that this is the only way to revitalize the nation. He also severely criticized the current decadence and romanticism of urban youth, hoping that Chinese youth will awaken as soon as possible, not forget the responsibilities of youth, and shoulder the great task of saving the nation. Mr. Zhang's speech lasted for about an hour. His sincere attitude and novel ideas moved all the listeners.

Wang Sisters' Tennis Performance

Grand Occasion in Bian

Quite Wonderful

(Kaifeng Correspondence) Wang sisters, famous national female tennis players, Chunxu and Chunxian, made their first performances in Bian today (9th) starting at 2 pm. Less than an hour beforehand, over a hundred people were waiting with their tickets. The Wang sisters, wearing white velvet coats, entered the stadium amidst audience applause at the strike of 2. Players from Bian, also in military attire, entered the stadium together. The performances began after a photo session. People thought it was already spectacular under their slight showing. Formally begun, first was the doubles match between Lu Xifen, Tong Zhiren against Wang sisters. The Wang sisters were overwhelming, taking two games in a row. Lu Xifen quickly revitalized, winning back one game. The Wang sisters won another game. Lu struck vehemently, making the Wang sisters run around to the point of exhaustion, winning four games in a row, then ended the match with 7 to 5. Lu Tong won. Second was the five-game match between Lu Xifen and Xu Zhonghui against Tong Zhiren and Chen Jingpan, which ended at three to two. Lu Xu won. Last was the mixed doubles match between Wang Chunqing and Xu Zhonghui against Wang Chunwei and Lu Xifen. Wang Lu won the first game with six to two. Wang Xu won the second game with six to three. The two sides competed fiercely in the last game. Wang Lu eventually won the final victory with eight to six. Overall, the two Wangs played wonderfully today. Both forehands and backhands were low and forceful. A'di's backhand was particularly good, often making Lu Xifen helpless. Lu Xifen was excellent at first, but afterwards she was probably tired from the long battle and did not play as well. Although Xu Zhonghui was flustered when she took the court, her clever drop shots today were quite unique. As for Chen Jingpan and Tong Zhiren, there was nothing spectacular. The two Wangs will leave Bian after tomorrow's performance. The results are as follows:

Lu Xifen, Tong Zhiren 7 - 5 Wang Chunqing, Wang Chunwei

Lu Xifen, Xu Zhonghui 2 - 2 Chen Jingpan, Tong Zhiren

Wang Chunxian, Lu Xifen 6 - 2, 3 - 6, 8 - 6 Wang Chunxu, Xu Zhong

Gold Market Closed on the Premier's Birthday

Gold Exchange Public Orders Extended to Today for Settlement

35 Orders to be Settled Today

63 Orders Still Unsettled

Yesterday was the Premier's birthday, and the gold exchange was closed for the day. All public orders for November were also postponed to today for settlement. The shorts had already settled 21 orders from Ding Tai and 14 orders from Da Feng Heng yesterday. Today, the longs should receive 14 orders from Shen Feng, 7 orders each from Da Chang Xiang, Yi Feng, and Yong Sheng, totaling 35 orders to be settled. The settlement price was 1136 yuan. Currently, there are 63 November orders still unsettled. The longs include 21 orders from Shen Feng, 14 orders from Da Chang Xiang, 7 orders each from Tian Feng, Fu An Sheng, Da Heng Xing, totaling 6 houses. The shorts include 35 orders from Ding Tai, 21 orders from Da Feng Heng, and 7 orders from Ding Kang, totaling 3 houses.

The Call Money Market Was Closed, and the Foreign Exchange Market Was Dull.

Chinese and Japanese Banks Were Nervously Purchasing.

The Hong Kong Market Was Initially Firm But Gradually Loosened.

The foreign exchange market yesterday started with strong purchases by Chinese merchants but weakened later. The Hong Kong market was firm. The process of the day was initially tight but loosened later. Early in the morning, overseas calls indicated that the London rate was close to the previous level but rose by 0.0625. The price of gold in London rose by one penny, the exchange rate between the pound and the US dollar narrowed by 0.125, and the exchange rate between the pound and the French franc fell by six pounds. The US market was completely closed, and market sentiment was still good. The exchange market opened in the morning with a selling price of one shilling and two pence 4375 for the near-term pound and 29.6875 yuan for the US dollar, which was 0.0625 tighter for the pound and unchanged for the US dollar compared to the previous close. After the opening, Chinese merchants continued to purchase strongly. Run Chang Yu and the Dalian group successively settled near-term and far-term US dollars, tightening the market. Although the Guangdong group provided some supply, it was minimal. Banks turned to buying, and the process became fixed. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation announced its exchange rates, which were unchanged for both the pound and the US dollar. The situation stabilized slightly. Later, although the Hong Kong market did not appear tight, Sassoon's settlement of shillings caused Japanese and Chinese merchants to purchase US dollars again, tightening the process. Swap rates also became more divergent. The Indian Silver Bureau predicted no change, and banks took advantage of the high prices to fill orders slightly, but the market softened at noon. The afternoon market was very mediocre and lacked change. Later, due to quiet buyers, Chinese merchants slightly settled the near-term rate, and the Hong Kong market firmed up and loosened. The initial report from the Indian Silver Bureau was a reduction of 5.5.5 Anna, which had little impact. The second telegram from the Indian Silver Bureau later stated no change, and the situation stabilized. Afterwards, trading became sparse and lacked support. Selling pressure became stronger, and the Hong Kong market continued to firm up and loosen. The closing selling price for the pound was one shilling and two pence 4375 and half a penny to match, and the US dollar was 29.6875 yuan, which was slightly softer compared to the previous close. Chinese merchants slightly purchased US dollars, about 200,000 yuan. Sassoon Japanese Bank Mobil also paid, and now the transaction price for the day will be recorded later.

The pound opened in the morning with a selling price of one shilling and two pence 4375 for the near term. HSBC sold 375 twelve-month contracts to Sassoon. Huabi bought 1875 January contracts. Lever Brothers B sold 3125 twelve-month contracts to Sassoon. McGarry C settled 25 twelve-month contracts. The noon closing price for the near term was one shilling and two pence 375. In the afternoon, British General C settled 3125 for the first half of December. HSBC sold 1875 January contracts to Korea. Korea resold 4375 to 鍙豐 for immediate delivery. The closing selling price for immediate delivery was one shilling and two pence 4375 and half a penny to match, 4375 for November, 3125 and 375 to match for December, 1875 and 25 to match for January, 0625 and 125 to match for February. The purchase price was increased by 0625.

The US dollar opened in the morning with a selling price of 29.6875 yuan for the near term. Lever Brothers B settled 625 November contracts. Huabi settled 375 December contracts. McGarry Citibank settled 0625 January contracts. HSBC sold 625 November contracts to Citibank. Citibank settled 375 December contracts and 29 yuan January contracts. HSBC sold to Mitsui at the same month and price. Huabi McGarry sold half a yuan to Zhenggin for November. Citibank settled 25 December contracts. McGarry settled 1875 for the same month. Huabi settled 8.875 yuan for January. The noon closing price for the near term was 29.4375 yuan. In the afternoon, Lever Brothers bought 29 yuan for January. Mitsubishi paid 8.9375 yuan and 29 yuan for the same month. Yarn and Cotton

The Recent Increase in Yarn and Cotton Prices

Yarn Up 30 Yuan, Cotton Up 10 Yuan

--And the Brand New Front Lines of Both Long and Short Positions--

The recent changes in the yarn and cotton market in the past two weeks have been rarely seen in history. The market has experienced a dramatic surge, completely affected by the gold market fluctuations. The call money market price has soared, reaching the third major threshold, passing 1,000 yuan, then exceeding 100 yuan, and then breaking through the 200 yuan threshold. New peaks have emerged endlessly, and the market sentiment has been greatly shaken. Rumors are rife, and there is no consensus. Group discussions focus on currency, and speculators are in a frenzy. Certain parties and banking circles are engaged in animal husbandry purchases. One cotton merchant has purchased as much as 70,000 bales of cotton and 14,500 bales of yarn at the highest. Mei Ji has also purchased about 30,000 bales of cotton. All of these are new purchases. Min Feng Yarn Factory and foreign merchants have the largest amount of short selling. In view of the tense situation, they are actively covering their positions, and the surge has continued. It is found that Chang Feng and Da Feng have the largest amount of short positions in cotton yarn, and they have successively purchased and tended to reverse to long positions. According to this movement, market prices will inevitably soar, and rumors are rampant for a time, soaring endlessly. It is found that the market price of standard yarn for October 15th of each month was between 173.4 yuan, and the price of standard cotton was about 33 yuan. Starting from the 16th, it began to rise until November 4th. The Ministry of Finance announced that the paper currency issued by the Central China Communications Bank is the legal currency, and cash may not be used. Therefore, the market situation was panic-stricken, and the buying frenzy was unprecedented. The opening price of the first board of each month broke through the 200 yuan threshold, and cotton all rushed out of the 40 yuan threshold. The far month jumped by 3 yuan to 43 yuan, and the December futures of standard yarn jumped by 6 yuan to 204 yuan, discovering the new peak since the abolition of taels and the change of yuan, which is an unprecedented new record since the establishment of the exchange, fully demonstrating the intensity of the surge. Subsequently, the bulls profited and sold, and the securities firms also sold, and the market price immediately plummeted. The December futures, which had the most intense surge, fell by 9 yuan from the peak. The difference in the rate on one day was as much as 9 yuan, fully demonstrating the chaos in the market. Later, the local authorities strictly prohibited rumors and raising prices, and all industries tended to be quiet, and the market gradually calmed down. The yarn market returned to normal. However, it is found that the bulls still do not underestimate the yarn and cotton market prices after the change of legal currency, and still adopt the strategy of buying on dips. Therefore, the bull's share is still concentrated and not released. The following is an excerpt of the recent lineup of standard yarn and cotton longs and shorts for reference:

Grain

No Difference Between the Northern and Southern Rice Markets

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of nearly 30 boats arrived from various sources (totaling over 6,000 stones of goods). Due to the cloudy weather, sellers' thoughts were ambiguous, and they shouted up prices as soon as they were listed. However, the sales market was sluggish, and the momentum was weak, and the situation was relaxed. Fortunately, the stomach bag was uninterrupted, and nearly a thousand bags were picked up from Tianjin, Yantai, Qingdao and other groups. The price of thin rice was able to stand, and the new japonica rice was also fixed. The supply and demand of Du Yangjian was equal, and there was no difference. However, the early rice from Nan'gang arrived in groups and sales were stagnant, and the depreciation fell to 角砠阴 and changed to 元 flat and flat. There was no difference in 破礱.

(North Shanghai) There were 37 or 38 sources, and the sales of various goods in the market were normal due to the cloudy and humid weather. The market prices of white japonica rice and Yangjian Du Jian埠尖客尖 were stable. Thin rice and late japonica rice were slightly soft, and other goods were the same as before.

Oil Market

New Asphalt Prices Seen to Rise

The new asphalt products from various producing areas have already been seen, but the products from the two groups of Han and Shanghai have not yet arrived. The Hankou market has to wait for the goods to be shipped from the E'xi Jingyi area, so the new asphalt product is seen later than in Shanghai. The existing stock in Hankou is still Chen oil, and the winter sales market has already started to move slightly. Because the cost of the Hakka is high, they are unwilling to sell at low prices. 重荆 must not be less than thirteen taels, and since the currency system has been improved, there is no need to worry about tightening of silver, so the Hakka's willingness to sell is even more firm. It is heard that there are only buyers and no sellers in recent days, so it must be added if you encounter a deal. The price of 麻城油 must also be twelve taels and five or six qian, and the price of 津市重砠 is probably more than thirteen taels. 本雄 traders never pay attention to 汉 in the early stage of new products, but rely on the new oil from the neighboring Zhejiang province for 注. It is heard that the new 本车油 from Jiaxing can be shipped on the same day, but the price has been taken over by the wholesale households on the spot, and the price has been increased by about two yuan, so the new oil is more expensive than the Chen oil. The market scale price of the 合到 Shanghai market is 19 yuan per tan. The traders are not convinced by such prices, so there are very few transactions. Generally, they are unwilling to pay the price unless it is urgent. However, the annual order is rich everywhere, but the new prices have risen, which is really unexpected.

White Tung Oil Turned from Decline to Sales

Since the new white tung oil was produced, the price has continued to fall, and it has been stable until the previous week. The lowest price sold by foreign firms in Hankou was 48 yuan in foreign regulations. Last week, the currency system was improved, and the loading and transportation in various producing areas could not help but wait and see, so the source of Hankou could not be prosperous. Although the spot oil transactions of various foreign firms were only dozens of tons, the arrival of goods was slightly scarce, and they showed a state of being insufficient for sales. The market has also turned tight, and the spot oil has been increased to 52 yuan and 10 cents per tan in foreign regulations. The futures oil for delivery in December is priced at 51 yuan. The total amount of futures and spot transactions is two or three tons. However, the currency system is now implemented everywhere, so the source of goods in the future will be prosperous day by day, and the market may fall slightly. However, the futures oil is now around 50 yuan, and even if it falls, it will be limited. In short, the key still depends on the prosperity of export trade.

Regular Meetings Held by the Personnel Management Society: National Personnel Management Conference 127

Including Order, Proposals, Speeches, Exhibitions, and Visits: Scheduled for Early February of Next Year in Shanghai

The Chinese Personnel Management Society held its 20th joint meeting of directors and supervisors yesterday at Rue Ratard. They also welcomed Mr. Che Gubingyuan, a director of the society, who had just returned from an overseas study tour. Those present included He Qingru, Zhang Sumin, Pan Yangyao, Yang Chongnie, Yang Weiyu, Shi Jiuyun, Tu Yinyin, Cao Yimin, and others. He Qingru chaired the meeting, with Wu Zongwen as the recorder. The following proposals were discussed: (1) It was resolved to hold a National Personnel Management Conference in Shanghai in early February of the 25th year. All institutions nationwide with personnel management departments may send representatives to attend and participate. The content will include proposals from various parties, speeches, visits, exhibitions, banquets, etc. (2) It was resolved that group discussions on personnel management issues will continue, and members are encouraged to participate.

Chinese District: Joint Meeting of Literacy Education Office 128

Over 800 Students from Literacy Schools in the District Attended: Representatives Gave Speeches and Entertainment Was Held

The Chinese District Office of the Municipal Literacy Education Committee, led by Director Jiang Menglin and Secretary Pan An, has shown great enthusiasm in promoting literacy. Recently, the 15 municipal literacy schools managed by the district office organized a joint meeting of students from all municipal literacy schools in the district at the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Corps yesterday afternoon at 6:00 PM, in order to train students' common sense of citizenship and promote friendship. In addition to over 800 students from various schools, there were also over 100 representatives from higher levels and guests. The meeting began at 6:30 PM with the ringing of a bell. After performing the rituals, Chairman Jiang Menglin reported the purpose and expectations of the meeting. This was followed by speeches from Huang Yaohua, representative of the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee, Wu Mengsheng, representative of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, Yang Xiaoqing, representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Yin Yong, Propaganda Committee Member of the district, and Lu Yin. Their words were mostly cautionary, moving all who listened. Entertainment began at 8:00 PM, with participation from various literacy schools, as well as performances from the Municipal Tangwan and Cangji Elementary Schools. Finally, educational films were shown. The event ended at 11:00 PM and was a great success.

International Education Society Holds Elementary School Student Literary Competition 130

Divided into Senior and Junior Grades: Results of the Assessment Will Be Announced Soon

The International Education Society, in order to encourage elementary school students' interest in literature, has specially organized a literary competition for elementary school students. The topic for senior grades is "My Opinions on Promoting International Friendship," and for junior grades, it is "The Individual I Admire the Most." Schools enthusiastically participated in the competition. The deadline for submissions was the end of this month, and over a hundred manuscripts were received. The announcement of the first and second-place winners will be made as soon as the assessment is completed.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Boy (93) 131

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Thank you, sir," Conn said, trying his best not to be rude, feeling it wasn't as difficult as he had thought.

"Now, let's take a look at that foot, ah-ha – this isn't good. We'll have to ask Dr. Field to come tomorrow. Shu, bring some hot water and gauze."

Mr. Pei washed and bandaged the injured foot. Mrs. Shu prepared the only empty bed in the house, which was located in the small parlor next to the sitting room. The children often used it when they were feeling unwell, as this saved Mrs. Shu from running up and down, and the patient wouldn't be lonely. Once the bed was ready, Mr. Pei carried the young boy in his arms, took him into the room, helped him undress, and placed him on the small white bed. Finally, he shook his hand and said in a fatherly manner, "I hope you sleep well tonight, my child," and then left.

Conn fell asleep immediately and slept soundly for several hours. Then his foot started throbbing again, and he woke up, tossing and turning, feeling extremely uneasy,忍着 not groaning to avoid being heard, because he was indeed a brave warrior, enduring the pain, truly like a "hero."

Mrs. Shu was accustomed to making nightly rounds of the entire house, so that if the wind was strong and the weather cold, she could close the windows, tidy up the mosquito net on Tandy's bed, and also take care of Tao Mo, because he sometimes got up and walked around in his sleep. The slightest sound could wake her. Sometimes she heard sounds that she thought were thieves, civet cats, or even a large fire. The doors of all the rooms were left open. So, that night, her sharp ears heard Conn's faint groans, and she immediately got up. He was disappointedly pounding his hot pillow when he suddenly saw a light flickering from the doorway, and then Mrs. Shu slipped into the room, looking like a funny ghost because her hair was tied into a bun in the center of her head, and she was dragging a long gray robe used for dressing behind her.
